Conditional Ibra and the Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on conditional ibra

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that ibra can be restricted by a condition but not suspended by a future event, and identify the mufta bihi position in the intra-Hanafi dispute.

Core Idea
Ibra can be restricted (with condition) but cannot be suspended (on future event) in Hanafi law.

This lesson delves into the nuanced distinction between conditional ibra (valid) and suspended ibra (invalid) in Hanafi fiqh. The passage presents five forms of conditional debt settlements and an intra-Hanafi disagreement between Abu Hanifa/Muhammad and Abu Yusuf. Understanding these forms is crucial for drafting valid debt compromises.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the distinction between restriction and suspension
Ibra can be restricted by a condition (e.g., 'on condition of payment tomorrow') but cannot be suspended by a future event (e.g., 'if you pay tomorrow'). The former makes the ibra effective only upon fulfillment; the latter is void.
The key is the wording: 'on condition' vs. 'if'.
2
Analyze the five forms
Go through each of the five forms from the text and determine whether the ibra is restricted or suspended. Note which form leads to the dispute.
3
Resolve the tarjih
State the position of the two (Abu Hanifa & Muhammad) and Abu Yusuf, and identify which is considered mufta bihi according to the commentator.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الصلح
الصلح في الدين
لا معاوضة، فلو صالح عن ألف على نصفه، أو على ألف مؤجل جاز، وعلى دنانير أي عن ألف حالة وهو خمسمائة صالح عن ألف حالة مؤجلة، أو عن ألف مؤجل أو سود على نصف حال أو بيض لا، ومن له على آخر عن النصف لا معاوضة: لأن مبادلة الأكثر بالأقل لا يجوز. (مسكين) فلو صالح إلخ: أي فلو صالح المديون دائنه عن ألف في ذمة على نصفه، وهو خمس مائة، أو على ألف مؤجل جاز الصلح في الوجهين، أما في الأول؛ فلأنه يجعل مستوفياً نصف حقه، ومسقطاً للنصف الآخر كما ذكرنا، وأما في الثاني، فكأنه أجل نفس الحق، ولا يحمل هذا على المعاوضة تحرزاً عن الربا؛ لأن بيع النقد بمثلها نسيئة لا يجوز إلا في قول للشافعي له أنه يجوز [رمز الحقائق: ٢٣٥/٢] ولو صالحه ألف جياد على خمس مائة زيوف حالة أو مؤجلة جاز؛ لأن من يستحق الجياد يستحق الزيوف، بخلاف عكسه، وهو ما إذا كان له ألف زيوف وصالحه على خمس مائة جياد حيث لا يجوز؛ لأنه لا يمكن حمله على أنه استوفى بعض حقه وأسقط الباقي؛ لأنه لا يستحق الجياد فيكون معاوضة ضرورة، فلا يجوز التفاضل، كذا في الزيلعي (فتح، عناية) أو على ألف مؤجل إلخ: وكذا لو صالحه عن ألف حالة على خمس مائة مؤجلة جاز كأنه أبرأه عن وأخر النصف كذا في الحموي. (فتح) وعلى دنانير مؤجّلة إلخ: أي ولو صالح عن ألف درهم حالة على دنانير مؤجلة، أو صالح عن ألف مؤجل على خمسمائة حالة، أو صالح عن ألف سود على خمسمائة بيض، وهو معنى قوله : على نصف حال، وهو يرجع إلى قوله : عن ألف مؤجل أي خمسمائة حالة، كما ذكرنا. وقوله: أو بيض يرجع إلى قوله: أو سود، والتقدير: على نصف بيض وهو بكسر الباء جمع بيضاء كعيس جمع عيساء، لا يجوز الصلح في الوجوه الثلاثة؛ لأن من له الدراهم لا يستحق الدنانير مؤجلة، ومن له دين مؤجل لا يستحق الحال، ومن له دراهم سود لا يستحق البيض؛ لأنها أجود، فيكون أخذها بطريق المعاوضة لا بطريق الاستيفاء. وشرط صحة المعاوضة في الجنس المتحد القدر المساواة ولم توجد فلهذا بطل الصلح، حتى لو صالحه على ألف حالة عن الألف الموجلة، أو صالحه على ألف بيض عن الألف السود جاز بشرط قبضه في المجلس؛ لوجود المساواة في القدر، وهو المعتبر في الصرف دون المساواة في الصفة، ولو كان عليه ألف فصالحه على طعام موصوف في الذمة مؤجل لم يجز؛ لأنه يكون افتراقا عن دين بدين، فلا يجوز.
ولو كان عليه ألف درهم ومائة دينار فصالحه على مائة درهم جاز سواء كانت حالة أو مؤجلة؛ لأنه يمكن أن يجعل إسقاطاً للدنانير كلها والدراهم إلا مائة وتأجيلاً للمائة التي بقيت فلا يحمل على المعاوضة؛ لأن فيه فساداً. [رمز الحقائق: ٢٣٥/٢، ٢٣٦] (فتح)
أو بيض: فيه لف ونشر، فالأول بالأول والثاني بالثاني. ومن له على آخر إلخ أي ومن له على آخر ألف درهم، فقال أي صاحب الألف لمن عليه الألف: أدّ إلي غداً نصفه أي نصف الألف، وهو خمسمائة على أنك بريء عن الفضل، وهو خمسمائة الباقية، ففعل من عليه الألف ذلك بأن أدى إليه في الغد خمسمائة برئ عن الفضل بالاتفاق؛ لأن الإبراء يحتمل التقييد بالشرط، وإن لم يحتمل التعليق به وكلمة "على" جعلت شرطاً؛ تصحيحاً لتصرفه، وإن كانت تستعمل للمعاوضة [رمز الحقائق: ٢٣٦/٢]
وإلا لا: أي وإن لم يؤد غداً النصف وهو خمسمائة، لا يبرأ عندهما، وقال أبو يوسف: يبرأ وإن لم يؤد، ولا تعود إليه الخمس مائة الساقطة أبداً؛ لأن اشتراط الأداء ضائع؛ لأن النقد واجب عليه في كل زمان يطالبه هو فيه؛ إذ المال حال عليه، فبطل التعليق، فصار إبراء مطلقاً، ولهما: أنه علق الإبراء بشرط، ولم يوجد. وهذه المسألة على وجوه الأول ما ذكرنا، والثاني: أن بالتقييد بأن يقول : صالحتك عن الألف على خمس مائة تدفعها إلي غداً، وأنت بريء من الزيادة على أنك إن لم تدفعها إلي غداً فلا تبرأ من الباقي، فيكون الأمر كما قال، والثالث: إذا قال: أبراتك من خمسمائة الألف على أن تعطيني خمس مائة غداً، فحكمه أنه يبرأ من وإن لم يؤد الخمسمائة في الغد. والرابع: أن يقول: أد إلي خمسمائة على أنك بريء من باقيه، ولم يوقت للأداء وقتاً، فحكمه أنه يبرأ مطلقاً؛ لأنه إبراء مطلق، والخامس: إذا قال: إن أديت إلي خمسمائة أو إذا أديت أو متى أديت، فحكمه أنه لا تعليق بالشرط صريحاً، والبراءة لا تحتمل التعليق بالشرط؛ لما فيها من معنى التمليك. [رمز الحقائق: ٢٣٦/٢] ووجه بطلان تعليق البراءة بالشرط: أن الإبراء إسقاط حتى لا يتوقف على القبول، وفيه معنى التمليك حتى يرتد بالرد، والتمليك لا يحتمل التعليق بالشرط والإسقاط يحتمل ذلك، فلمعنى التمليك قلنا: إذا صرح بالشرط لم يصح، ولمعنى الإسقاط إذا لم يصرح بالشرط يتقيد كذا في "عربي زاده". (فتح) قال لآخر إلخ: أي ومن قال لآخر : لا أقر لك بمالك علي حتى تؤخره أي مالك عني، يعني تؤجله، أو تحط عنه بعضه، ففعل الدائن ذلك، أما إن أخره أو حط عنه بعضه، صح هذا الفعل عليه أي على الدائن، يعني إن أخره يتأخر عنه، وإن حط عنه بعضه ينحط؛ لأن المديون ليس بمكره، فصار هذا نظير الصلح مع الإنكار، وعند الثلاثة: لا [رمز الحقائق: ٢٣٦/٢، ٢٣٧] يصح.
ومن تحط يعني صح: أي لزمه، وليس للدائن أن يطالب المديون في الحال وبما حط، هذا إذا قاله سراً حتى إذا قال علانية بحضور الشهود يؤخذ المقر بالمال في الحال ملا مسكين وقال في "حاشية فتح المعين": لأنه ليس بمكره؛ لتمكنه من إقامة البيئة أو التحليف، فينكل، وهو نظير الصلح مع الإنكار؛ فكان مختاراً في تصرفه، أقصى ما في الباب أنه مضطر، لكن الاضطرار لا يمنع من نفوذ تصرفه كبيع ماله بالطعام عند المخمصة [تبيين الحقائق: ٤٩٧/٥]
Book of Compromise. Compromise concerning debt is not an exchange. So if one settles a debt of one thousand for half of it, or for one thousand deferred, it is valid. And with dinars, i.e., for one thousand present and it is five hundred, he settled for one thousand present deferred, or for one thousand deferred or black dirhams for half present or white dirhams, it is not valid. And from one who has against another... "Not an exchange" because exchanging more for less is not permissible. (Miskin) "So if he settles etc.": i.e., if the debtor settles with his creditor for one thousand in the debt for half of it, which is five hundred, or for one thousand deferred, the settlement is valid in both ways. As for the first, because he is considered to have received half of his right and dropped the other half as we mentioned. As for the second, it is as if he deferred the right itself. And this is not considered an exchange to avoid riba, because selling cash for the same on credit is not permissible except in one saying of al-Shafi'i that he deems it permissible. [Hashiya: 2:235] And if he settles with him one thousand good dirhams for five hundred counterfeit dirhams, present or deferred, it is valid, because one who deserves good dirhams deserves counterfeit ones. Unlike its opposite, which is if he had one thousand counterfeit dirhams and settled for five hundred good dirhams, where it is not valid, because it cannot be considered as him having received part of his right and dropped the rest, because he does not deserve good dirhams, so it becomes necessarily an exchange, and thus disparity is not permissible. As in al-Zayla'i. (Fath, Inayah) "Or for one thousand deferred etc.": Similarly, if he settled with him for one thousand present for five hundred deferred, it is valid, as if he released him from half and deferred half. As in al-Hamawi. (Fath) "And for deferred dinars etc.": i.e., if he settled for one thousand present dirhams for deferred dinars, or settled for one thousand deferred for five hundred present, or settled for one thousand black dirhams for five hundred white dirhams, which is the meaning of his saying "for half present" and it refers to his saying "for one thousand deferred" i.e., five hundred present, as we mentioned. And his saying "or white" refers to his saying "or black", and the estimation is: for half white — with kasra of the ba, plural of bayda like 'is plural of 'aisa. It is not valid in the three ways because the one who has dirhams does not deserve deferred dinars, the one who has a deferred debt does not deserve present, and the one who has black dirhams does not deserve white because they are better quality, so taking them is by way of exchange, not by way of receipt. And the condition for validity of exchange in a single genus is equality in amount, and it was not found, so the settlement is void. So if he settled with him for one thousand present for the one thousand deferred, or settled for one thousand white for one thousand black, it is valid on condition of taking possession in the session, because equality in amount is found, and that is what matters in sarf, not equality in quality. And if he owed one thousand and settled for described food in the debt deferred, it is not valid, because it would be parting from a debt for a debt, and it is not permissible. And if he owed one thousand dirhams and one hundred dinars, and settled for one hundred dirhams, it is valid, whether present or deferred, because it can be considered as dropping all the dinars and the dirhams except one hundred, and deferring the remaining one hundred, so it is not considered an exchange because that would be corruption. [Hashiya: 2:235-236] (Fath) "Or white": there is laff wa nashr, the first with the first and the second with the second. "And from one who has against another etc.": i.e., and from one who has against another one thousand dirhams, and he said — i.e., the owner of the thousand to the one who owes him: Pay me tomorrow half of it, i.e., half of the thousand, which is five hundred, on the condition that you are free from the remainder, which is the remaining five hundred. So the one who owes the thousand did that, i.e., paid him the five hundred tomorrow, he becomes free from the remainder by agreement, because ibra (remission) can be restricted by a condition, though it cannot be suspended by one, and the word 'ala (on condition) is made a condition to validate his action, even though it is used for exchange. [Hashiya: 2:236] "Otherwise no": i.e., if he did not pay the half (five hundred) tomorrow, he does not become free according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad). Abu Yusuf said: he becomes free even if he did not pay, and the five hundred dropped never revert, because stipulating payment is futile, since the payment was incumbent on him at every time the creditor demands, because the money was due, so the suspension is void, and it becomes an absolute ibra. According to the two: he suspended the ibra on a condition, and it did not occur. This issue has several forms: the first is what we mentioned. The second: with restriction, such as saying: I settle with you for the thousand for five hundred you pay me tomorrow, and you are free from the excess, on condition that if you do not pay it tomorrow, you are not free from the remainder; then it is as he said. The third: if he said: I grant you ibra from five hundred of the thousand on condition that you give me five hundred tomorrow; his ruling is that he is free even if he does not pay the five hundred tomorrow. The fourth: if he said: Pay me five hundred on condition that you are free from the remainder, and he did not set a time for payment; his ruling is that he is free absolutely, because it is an absolute ibra. The fifth: if he said: If you pay me five hundred, or when you pay me, or whenever you pay me; his ruling is that there is no explicit suspension by condition, and ibra cannot be suspended by condition because it contains the meaning of ownership. [Hashiya: 2:236] And the reason for the invalidity of suspending ibra by a condition is that ibra is a dropping (isqat) so it does not depend on acceptance, but it has the meaning of ownership so it can be revoked by rejection, and ownership cannot be suspended by a condition while dropping can. So due to the meaning of ownership, we say: if he explicitly makes a condition, it is not valid; and due to the meaning of dropping, if he does not explicitly make a condition, it is restricted. As in 'Arabi Zada. (Fath) "He said to another etc.": i.e., and from one who said to another: I do not acknowledge that you have a debt against me until you defer it from me — meaning you defer it, or drop part of it. So the creditor did that, if he deferred it or dropped part of it, this action is valid upon him, i.e., upon the creditor, meaning if he deferred it, it is deferred, and if he dropped part of it, it drops, because the debtor was not coerced, so this is analogous to sulh with denial. According to the three, it is not valid. [Hashiya: 2:236-237] "And from one who drops means valid": i.e., it is binding, and the creditor cannot demand the debtor immediately nor for what was dropped. This is if he said it secretly, but if he said it openly in front of witnesses, the one who acknowledges the debt is taken for the debt immediately. Mulla Miskin said in Hashiyat Fath al-Mu'in: because he is not coerced, as he can produce evidence or take an oath, and he would be reluctant; it is analogous to sulh with denial, so he is free in his action. At most, he is compelled, but compulsion does not prevent the effectiveness of his action, like selling his property for food during famine. [Tabyin al-Haqa'iq: 5:497]
Source pages p. 83

Commentary
This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq is a ruling statement with commentary explaining the fiqh of compromise (sulh) in debts. The central principle is that sulh in debt is not a sale or exchange (mu'awada) but rather a remission (ibra) or deferment, to avoid riba (usury). The author first states the general rule: settling a debt of 1000 for 500 (half) or for 1000 deferred is valid. The commentary clarifies why: in the first case, it is as if the creditor simply forgives half; in the second, he defers the whole. If it were considered an exchange of more for less, it would be riba. The text then addresses various scenarios: settling good dirhams for counterfeit (valid) but not the reverse; settling deferred debt for immediate payment (valid) and vice versa; settling black dirhams for white (invalid unless equality of amount); and settling debt for deferred food (invalid because it is a debt for a debt). A key point is that in sarf (exchange of same genus), equality of amount is required, not quality. The second part discusses a conditional settlement: a debtor says 'Pay me 500 tomorrow and you are free from the remaining 500.' If he pays on time, he is free by agreement. If not, Abu Hanifa and Muhammad hold he remains liable, while Abu Yusuf considers him free because the condition is void. The text elaborates five forms of conditional ibra. Finally, it discusses a case where a debtor under pressure acknowledges a debt conditionally; if done secretly, it is valid, but if done openly, it is not binding. Throughout, the ruling is based on the Hanafi position that ibra can be restricted (by condition) but not suspended (by a future event).

Key Terms
الإبراء (al-ibra): Legal discharge or remission of a debt without compensation.
التقييد (al-taqyid): Restriction: making ibra conditional on a future event in a way that it takes effect only if the event occurs.
التعليق (al-ta'liq): Suspension: making ibra dependent on a future event in a way that it is not effective until the event occurs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi school, which of the following statements would make a valid conditional ibra (i.e., ibra takes effect only if the condition is met)?
A) 'I forgive your debt if you pay me 500 tomorrow.'
B) 'I forgive your debt on condition that you pay me 500 tomorrow.'
C) 'I forgive half your debt, and if you pay the other half tomorrow, I forgive the rest.'
D) 'I grant you ibra from the entire debt when you pay me 500 tomorrow.'

Key Takeaway
Ibra can be restricted by a condition (e.g., 'on condition of payment') but cannot be suspended by a future event (e.g., 'if you pay'). The mufta bihi follows Abu Hanifa and Muhammad: condition must be fulfilled.

Debtor's Conditional Acknowledgment Under Pressure
Ruling on debtor's conditional acknowledgment under duress

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to determine when a debtor's conditional acknowledgment of a debt under pressure is binding and when it is not.

Core Idea
A debtor's conditional acknowledgment made secretly is valid; made openly, it is invalid because coercion is not established.

The final section of the passage addresses a specific scenario: a debtor says he will not acknowledge a debt unless the creditor defers or reduces it. If the creditor agrees, the modification is binding on the creditor if done secretly, but not if done openly. This ruling is analogous to sulh with denial (sulh ma'a al-inkar).

Guided Path
1
Differentiate secret vs open
If the debtor makes the statement secretly (without witnesses), the creditor's agreement is binding because the debtor appears coerced. If open, the debtor could have defended himself, so the acknowledgment is not binding.
The key is the presence of witnesses.
2
Apply the analogy to sulh with denial
This case is compared to sulh with denial, where a person pays to avoid litigation; his action is valid because he is not coerced but chooses to settle.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الصلح
الصلح في الدين
لا معاوضة، فلو صالح عن ألف على نصفه، أو على ألف مؤجل جاز، وعلى دنانير أي عن ألف حالة وهو خمسمائة صالح عن ألف حالة مؤجلة، أو عن ألف مؤجل أو سود على نصف حال أو بيض لا، ومن له على آخر عن النصف لا معاوضة: لأن مبادلة الأكثر بالأقل لا يجوز. (مسكين) فلو صالح إلخ: أي فلو صالح المديون دائنه عن ألف في ذمة على نصفه، وهو خمس مائة، أو على ألف مؤجل جاز الصلح في الوجهين، أما في الأول؛ فلأنه يجعل مستوفياً نصف حقه، ومسقطاً للنصف الآخر كما ذكرنا، وأما في الثاني، فكأنه أجل نفس الحق، ولا يحمل هذا على المعاوضة تحرزاً عن الربا؛ لأن بيع النقد بمثلها نسيئة لا يجوز إلا في قول للشافعي له أنه يجوز [رمز الحقائق: ٢٣٥/٢] ولو صالحه ألف جياد على خمس مائة زيوف حالة أو مؤجلة جاز؛ لأن من يستحق الجياد يستحق الزيوف، بخلاف عكسه، وهو ما إذا كان له ألف زيوف وصالحه على خمس مائة جياد حيث لا يجوز؛ لأنه لا يمكن حمله على أنه استوفى بعض حقه وأسقط الباقي؛ لأنه لا يستحق الجياد فيكون معاوضة ضرورة، فلا يجوز التفاضل، كذا في الزيلعي (فتح، عناية) أو على ألف مؤجل إلخ: وكذا لو صالحه عن ألف حالة على خمس مائة مؤجلة جاز كأنه أبرأه عن وأخر النصف كذا في الحموي. (فتح) وعلى دنانير مؤجّلة إلخ: أي ولو صالح عن ألف درهم حالة على دنانير مؤجلة، أو صالح عن ألف مؤجل على خمسمائة حالة، أو صالح عن ألف سود على خمسمائة بيض، وهو معنى قوله : على نصف حال، وهو يرجع إلى قوله : عن ألف مؤجل أي خمسمائة حالة، كما ذكرنا. وقوله: أو بيض يرجع إلى قوله: أو سود، والتقدير: على نصف بيض وهو بكسر الباء جمع بيضاء كعيس جمع عيساء، لا يجوز الصلح في الوجوه الثلاثة؛ لأن من له الدراهم لا يستحق الدنانير مؤجلة، ومن له دين مؤجل لا يستحق الحال، ومن له دراهم سود لا يستحق البيض؛ لأنها أجود، فيكون أخذها بطريق المعاوضة لا بطريق الاستيفاء. وشرط صحة المعاوضة في الجنس المتحد القدر المساواة ولم توجد فلهذا بطل الصلح، حتى لو صالحه على ألف حالة عن الألف الموجلة، أو صالحه على ألف بيض عن الألف السود جاز بشرط قبضه في المجلس؛ لوجود المساواة في القدر، وهو المعتبر في الصرف دون المساواة في الصفة، ولو كان عليه ألف فصالحه على طعام موصوف في الذمة مؤجل لم يجز؛ لأنه يكون افتراقا عن دين بدين، فلا يجوز.
ولو كان عليه ألف درهم ومائة دينار فصالحه على مائة درهم جاز سواء كانت حالة أو مؤجلة؛ لأنه يمكن أن يجعل إسقاطاً للدنانير كلها والدراهم إلا مائة وتأجيلاً للمائة التي بقيت فلا يحمل على المعاوضة؛ لأن فيه فساداً. [رمز الحقائق: ٢٣٥/٢، ٢٣٦] (فتح)
أو بيض: فيه لف ونشر، فالأول بالأول والثاني بالثاني. ومن له على آخر إلخ أي ومن له على آخر ألف درهم، فقال أي صاحب الألف لمن عليه الألف: أدّ إلي غداً نصفه أي نصف الألف، وهو خمسمائة على أنك بريء عن الفضل، وهو خمسمائة الباقية، ففعل من عليه الألف ذلك بأن أدى إليه في الغد خمسمائة برئ عن الفضل بالاتفاق؛ لأن الإبراء يحتمل التقييد بالشرط، وإن لم يحتمل التعليق به وكلمة "على" جعلت شرطاً؛ تصحيحاً لتصرفه، وإن كانت تستعمل للمعاوضة [رمز الحقائق: ٢٣٦/٢]
وإلا لا: أي وإن لم يؤد غداً النصف وهو خمسمائة، لا يبرأ عندهما، وقال أبو يوسف: يبرأ وإن لم يؤد، ولا تعود إليه الخمس مائة الساقطة أبداً؛ لأن اشتراط الأداء ضائع؛ لأن النقد واجب عليه في كل زمان يطالبه هو فيه؛ إذ المال حال عليه، فبطل التعليق، فصار إبراء مطلقاً، ولهما: أنه علق الإبراء بشرط، ولم يوجد. وهذه المسألة على وجوه الأول ما ذكرنا، والثاني: أن بالتقييد بأن يقول : صالحتك عن الألف على خمس مائة تدفعها إلي غداً، وأنت بريء من الزيادة على أنك إن لم تدفعها إلي غداً فلا تبرأ من الباقي، فيكون الأمر كما قال، والثالث: إذا قال: أبراتك من خمسمائة الألف على أن تعطيني خمس مائة غداً، فحكمه أنه يبرأ من وإن لم يؤد الخمسمائة في الغد. والرابع: أن يقول: أد إلي خمسمائة على أنك بريء من باقيه، ولم يوقت للأداء وقتاً، فحكمه أنه يبرأ مطلقاً؛ لأنه إبراء مطلق، والخامس: إذا قال: إن أديت إلي خمسمائة أو إذا أديت أو متى أديت، فحكمه أنه لا تعليق بالشرط صريحاً، والبراءة لا تحتمل التعليق بالشرط؛ لما فيها من معنى التمليك. [رمز الحقائق: ٢٣٦/٢] ووجه بطلان تعليق البراءة بالشرط: أن الإبراء إسقاط حتى لا يتوقف على القبول، وفيه معنى التمليك حتى يرتد بالرد، والتمليك لا يحتمل التعليق بالشرط والإسقاط يحتمل ذلك، فلمعنى التمليك قلنا: إذا صرح بالشرط لم يصح، ولمعنى الإسقاط إذا لم يصرح بالشرط يتقيد كذا في "عربي زاده". (فتح) قال لآخر إلخ: أي ومن قال لآخر : لا أقر لك بمالك علي حتى تؤخره أي مالك عني، يعني تؤجله، أو تحط عنه بعضه، ففعل الدائن ذلك، أما إن أخره أو حط عنه بعضه، صح هذا الفعل عليه أي على الدائن، يعني إن أخره يتأخر عنه، وإن حط عنه بعضه ينحط؛ لأن المديون ليس بمكره، فصار هذا نظير الصلح مع الإنكار، وعند الثلاثة: لا [رمز الحقائق: ٢٣٦/٢، ٢٣٧] يصح.
ومن تحط يعني صح: أي لزمه، وليس للدائن أن يطالب المديون في الحال وبما حط، هذا إذا قاله سراً حتى إذا قال علانية بحضور الشهود يؤخذ المقر بالمال في الحال ملا مسكين وقال في "حاشية فتح المعين": لأنه ليس بمكره؛ لتمكنه من إقامة البيئة أو التحليف، فينكل، وهو نظير الصلح مع الإنكار؛ فكان مختاراً في تصرفه، أقصى ما في الباب أنه مضطر، لكن الاضطرار لا يمنع من نفوذ تصرفه كبيع ماله بالطعام عند المخمصة [تبيين الحقائق: ٤٩٧/٥]
Book of Compromise. Compromise concerning debt is not an exchange. So if one settles a debt of one thousand for half of it, or for one thousand deferred, it is valid. And with dinars, i.e., for one thousand present and it is five hundred, he settled for one thousand present deferred, or for one thousand deferred or black dirhams for half present or white dirhams, it is not valid. And from one who has against another... "Not an exchange" because exchanging more for less is not permissible. (Miskin) "So if he settles etc.": i.e., if the debtor settles with his creditor for one thousand in the debt for half of it, which is five hundred, or for one thousand deferred, the settlement is valid in both ways. As for the first, because he is considered to have received half of his right and dropped the other half as we mentioned. As for the second, it is as if he deferred the right itself. And this is not considered an exchange to avoid riba, because selling cash for the same on credit is not permissible except in one saying of al-Shafi'i that he deems it permissible. [Hashiya: 2:235] And if he settles with him one thousand good dirhams for five hundred counterfeit dirhams, present or deferred, it is valid, because one who deserves good dirhams deserves counterfeit ones. Unlike its opposite, which is if he had one thousand counterfeit dirhams and settled for five hundred good dirhams, where it is not valid, because it cannot be considered as him having received part of his right and dropped the rest, because he does not deserve good dirhams, so it becomes necessarily an exchange, and thus disparity is not permissible. As in al-Zayla'i. (Fath, Inayah) "Or for one thousand deferred etc.": Similarly, if he settled with him for one thousand present for five hundred deferred, it is valid, as if he released him from half and deferred half. As in al-Hamawi. (Fath) "And for deferred dinars etc.": i.e., if he settled for one thousand present dirhams for deferred dinars, or settled for one thousand deferred for five hundred present, or settled for one thousand black dirhams for five hundred white dirhams, which is the meaning of his saying "for half present" and it refers to his saying "for one thousand deferred" i.e., five hundred present, as we mentioned. And his saying "or white" refers to his saying "or black", and the estimation is: for half white — with kasra of the ba, plural of bayda like 'is plural of 'aisa. It is not valid in the three ways because the one who has dirhams does not deserve deferred dinars, the one who has a deferred debt does not deserve present, and the one who has black dirhams does not deserve white because they are better quality, so taking them is by way of exchange, not by way of receipt. And the condition for validity of exchange in a single genus is equality in amount, and it was not found, so the settlement is void. So if he settled with him for one thousand present for the one thousand deferred, or settled for one thousand white for one thousand black, it is valid on condition of taking possession in the session, because equality in amount is found, and that is what matters in sarf, not equality in quality. And if he owed one thousand and settled for described food in the debt deferred, it is not valid, because it would be parting from a debt for a debt, and it is not permissible. And if he owed one thousand dirhams and one hundred dinars, and settled for one hundred dirhams, it is valid, whether present or deferred, because it can be considered as dropping all the dinars and the dirhams except one hundred, and deferring the remaining one hundred, so it is not considered an exchange because that would be corruption. [Hashiya: 2:235-236] (Fath) "Or white": there is laff wa nashr, the first with the first and the second with the second. "And from one who has against another etc.": i.e., and from one who has against another one thousand dirhams, and he said — i.e., the owner of the thousand to the one who owes him: Pay me tomorrow half of it, i.e., half of the thousand, which is five hundred, on the condition that you are free from the remainder, which is the remaining five hundred. So the one who owes the thousand did that, i.e., paid him the five hundred tomorrow, he becomes free from the remainder by agreement, because ibra (remission) can be restricted by a condition, though it cannot be suspended by one, and the word 'ala (on condition) is made a condition to validate his action, even though it is used for exchange. [Hashiya: 2:236] "Otherwise no": i.e., if he did not pay the half (five hundred) tomorrow, he does not become free according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad). Abu Yusuf said: he becomes free even if he did not pay, and the five hundred dropped never revert, because stipulating payment is futile, since the payment was incumbent on him at every time the creditor demands, because the money was due, so the suspension is void, and it becomes an absolute ibra. According to the two: he suspended the ibra on a condition, and it did not occur. This issue has several forms: the first is what we mentioned. The second: with restriction, such as saying: I settle with you for the thousand for five hundred you pay me tomorrow, and you are free from the excess, on condition that if you do not pay it tomorrow, you are not free from the remainder; then it is as he said. The third: if he said: I grant you ibra from five hundred of the thousand on condition that you give me five hundred tomorrow; his ruling is that he is free even if he does not pay the five hundred tomorrow. The fourth: if he said: Pay me five hundred on condition that you are free from the remainder, and he did not set a time for payment; his ruling is that he is free absolutely, because it is an absolute ibra. The fifth: if he said: If you pay me five hundred, or when you pay me, or whenever you pay me; his ruling is that there is no explicit suspension by condition, and ibra cannot be suspended by condition because it contains the meaning of ownership. [Hashiya: 2:236] And the reason for the invalidity of suspending ibra by a condition is that ibra is a dropping (isqat) so it does not depend on acceptance, but it has the meaning of ownership so it can be revoked by rejection, and ownership cannot be suspended by a condition while dropping can. So due to the meaning of ownership, we say: if he explicitly makes a condition, it is not valid; and due to the meaning of dropping, if he does not explicitly make a condition, it is restricted. As in 'Arabi Zada. (Fath) "He said to another etc.": i.e., and from one who said to another: I do not acknowledge that you have a debt against me until you defer it from me — meaning you defer it, or drop part of it. So the creditor did that, if he deferred it or dropped part of it, this action is valid upon him, i.e., upon the creditor, meaning if he deferred it, it is deferred, and if he dropped part of it, it drops, because the debtor was not coerced, so this is analogous to sulh with denial. According to the three, it is not valid. [Hashiya: 2:236-237] "And from one who drops means valid": i.e., it is binding, and the creditor cannot demand the debtor immediately nor for what was dropped. This is if he said it secretly, but if he said it openly in front of witnesses, the one who acknowledges the debt is taken for the debt immediately. Mulla Miskin said in Hashiyat Fath al-Mu'in: because he is not coerced, as he can produce evidence or take an oath, and he would be reluctant; it is analogous to sulh with denial, so he is free in his action. At most, he is compelled, but compulsion does not prevent the effectiveness of his action, like selling his property for food during famine. [Tabyin al-Haqa'iq: 5:497]
Source pages p. 83

Commentary
This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq is a ruling statement with commentary explaining the fiqh of compromise (sulh) in debts. The central principle is that sulh in debt is not a sale or exchange (mu'awada) but rather a remission (ibra) or deferment, to avoid riba (usury). The author first states the general rule: settling a debt of 1000 for 500 (half) or for 1000 deferred is valid. The commentary clarifies why: in the first case, it is as if the creditor simply forgives half; in the second, he defers the whole. If it were considered an exchange of more for less, it would be riba. The text then addresses various scenarios: settling good dirhams for counterfeit (valid) but not the reverse; settling deferred debt for immediate payment (valid) and vice versa; settling black dirhams for white (invalid unless equality of amount); and settling debt for deferred food (invalid because it is a debt for a debt). A key point is that in sarf (exchange of same genus), equality of amount is required, not quality. The second part discusses a conditional settlement: a debtor says 'Pay me 500 tomorrow and you are free from the remaining 500.' If he pays on time, he is free by agreement. If not, Abu Hanifa and Muhammad hold he remains liable, while Abu Yusuf considers him free because the condition is void. The text elaborates five forms of conditional ibra. Finally, it discusses a case where a debtor under pressure acknowledges a debt conditionally; if done secretly, it is valid, but if done openly, it is not binding. Throughout, the ruling is based on the Hanafi position that ibra can be restricted (by condition) but not suspended (by a future event).

Key Terms
إكراه (ikrah): Legal duress or coercion that invalidates a transaction.
اضطرار (idtirar): Compulsion or necessity; a person acts under pressure but with some choice.
الصلح مع الإنكار (al-sulh ma'a al-inkar): A compromise settlement where the debtor denies the debt but pays to avoid litigation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A debtor privately tells his creditor: 'I won't admit I owe you unless you defer the payment by a year.' The creditor agrees. According to Hanafi fiqh, what is the ruling?
A) The deferral is valid and binding on the creditor.
B) The deferral is invalid because the debtor was coerced.
C) The debtor must still pay immediately.
D) The deferral is valid only if witnessed.

Key Takeaway
A debtor's conditional acknowledgment under pressure is valid if made secretly; if made openly, it is not binding.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
8 min
Joint Debt: Partner's Settlement for a Specific Item
Explains rulings for joint debt when one partner compromises his share for an item

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the options available to a partner when one partner settles his share of a joint debt for a specific item, and apply the conditions that determine the validity of participation.

Core Idea
A partner who settles his share of a joint debt for a specific item does not exclude his copartner from sharing that item, unless the settlement is treated as a complete exchange.

Joint debt (dayn mushtarak) arises from a single cause, such as a joint sale or inheritance. When one partner compromises his share for a specific asset, a conflict arises between the rights of the partners. This lesson from Kanz al-Daqa'iq explains the options of the other partner and the conditions that govern participation, using istihsan to balance competing interests.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Its Ruling
The act is the settlement (sulh) by one partner of his share of a joint debt for a specific item (e.g., a garment). The ruling: the settlement is valid, but the other partner has a choice (khiyar) to either pursue the debtor or take half the item from the settling partner.
This applies only when the settled matter is a debt, not a specific physical asset.
2
Trace the Dalil and Wajh al-Dalalah
The text uses istihsan (equity) to allow participation. The chain: joint debt cannot be divided before receipt; the substitute (the garment) stands in for the undivided share. Therefore, the other partner has a right to share it, unless harm would result.
The dalil is implied through qiyas khafi: comparison to cases where division would cause harm.
3
Examine the Conditions and Distinctions
Two key conditions: (1) The settled matter must be a debt (not a specific joint asset); (2) the substitute must be of a different genus than the debt. If the substitute is of the same genus, the partner participates fully; if the settlement is for a specific joint asset, no participation.
The text also notes that there is no difference whether the settlement was by acknowledgment, silence, or denial.
4
Note the Ikhtilaf in the Salam Contract
When two parties have given salam (advance payment) for a commodity and one settles his share for the capital, Abu Hanifa and Muhammad hold it is suspended (mawquf) pending the other's permission. Abu Yusuf allows it immediately.
This dispute arises from differing views on the divisibility of the salam obligation.
5
Determine the Mufta Bihi
The relied-upon position is the suspended view (mawquf), as per al-Fath and most later authorities. Therefore, the settlement is not effective unless the other partner permits.

Source Text

كتاب الصلح
فصل
الدين المشترك
دين بينهما صالح أحدهما عن نصيبه على ثوب، لشريكه أن يتبع المديون بنصفه، أو يأخذ نصف الثوب من شريكه إلا أن يضمن ربع الدين ولو قبض نصيبه شركه فيه ورجعا بالباقي على الغريم،

فصل: هذا فصل في الدين المشترك، وهو ما حصل بسبب متحد، كما لو باعا عبداً مشتركاً صفقة واحدة، أو استهلكه إنسان، أو كان الدين ميراثاً بين الورثة. (مسكين) دين بينهما إلخ [أخر الدين المشترك عن المفرد؛ لأن المثنى بعد الواحد. (فتح)] أي دين مشترك بين اثنين الشريكين، والدين المشترك أن يكون واجباً بسبب متحد كثمن المبيع، وقيمة العين المشتركة المستهلكة، وبدل القرض من المال المشترك بينهما، والموروث بين اثنين، صالح أحدهما أي أحد الشريكين المديون عن نصيبه من الدين على ثوب، فلشريكه الخيار إن شاء أن يتبع المديون بنصفه أي بنصف الدين لبقاء حصة في ذمته أو يأخذ نصف الثوب من شريكه؛ لأن له حق المشاركة؛ لأنه عوض عن دينه. [رمز الحقائق: ٢٣٧/٢]
إلا أن يضمن إلخ: وفي بعض النسخ: يضمنه، أي يضمن الشريك المصالح ربع الدين؛ لأن حقه في الدين لا في الثوب، ولا فرق فيه بين أن يكون الصلح عن إقرار أو عن سكوت أو عن إنكار ، ثم ههنا قيدان آخران الأول: أن يكون المصالح عنه ديناً؛ لأنه لو كان الصلح عن عين مشتركة يختص المصالح ببدل الصلح، وليس لشريكه أن يشاركه فيه؛ لكونه معاوضة من كل وجه؛ لأن المصالح. عنه مال حقيقة بخلاف الدين والثاني: أن يكون المصالح عليه ثوباً، والمراد خلاف جنس الدين؛ لأنه لو صالحه على جنسه يشاركه فيه، ويرجعان على المديون، وليس للقابض فيه خيار ؛ لأنه بمنزلة قبض بعض الدين رمز الحقائق: ۲۳۷/۲]
ولو قبض نصيبه إلخ: أي ولو قبض أحد الشريكين نصيبه شركه الشريك الآخر. (مسكين) وقال في "الفتح": لأن قسمة الدين لا تتصور والمقبوض بدل عنه فله أن يشاركه فيه؛ لكونه عين حقه من وجه، بخلاف ما إذا اشترى به ثوباً حيث لا يشاركه فيه؛ لأنه مبادلة من كل وجه، وإنما كان له أن يشاركه في الثوب في فصل الصلح كي لا يلزم المصالح الضرر ولو سلم المقبوض واختار متابعة الغريم ثم مات الغريم، رجع على القابض بنصف ما قبض؛ لأن التسليم مقيد بشرط سلامة الباقي، لكن ليس له أن يرجع في عين تلك الدراهم المقبوضة؛ لأن حقه فيها قد سقط بالتسليم فلا يعود حقه فيها بالتوى، ويعود إلى ذمة في مثلها كذا في "الزيلعي"، ومنه يعلم ما في "العيني" من الخلل. فتح المعين ورجعا إلخ : أي الشريكان بالباقي من الدين على الغريم، وهو المديون؛ لأن قسمة الدين لا تتصوّر في الذمة قبل القبض والقبض بدل عنه، فله أن يشاركه فيه إن شاء؛ لأنه . حقه عين

كتاب الصلح
الدين المشترك
ولو اشترى بنصيبه شيئا، ضمنه ربع الدين، وبطل صلح أحد ربي السلم من نصيبه
أي أحدهما
ضمن الشريك المشتري
أحد الشريكين في السلم
من وجه وإن شاء رجع على الغريم وهو المديون؛ لأن حقه عليه في الحقيقة، وإنما كان له أن يشاركه في فضل الثوب في فصل الصلح؛ كي لا يلزم المصالح الضرر ، وههنا انتفى الضرر فيرجع بربع الدين، ثم يرجعان على الغريم؛ لاستوائهما في الاقتضاء، ولو سلم له المقبوض واختار متابعة الغريم ثم توى نصيبه بأن مات الغريم مفلساً، رجع على القابض بنصف ما قبض؛ لأن التسليم مقيد بشرط سلامة الباقي له، فإذا لم يسلم له رجع عليه كما في الحوالة رمز الحقائق: ۲۳۷/۲]
لأن
ربع
ولو اشترى إلخ أي لو اشترى أحد الشريكين من الذي عليه الدين بنصيبه من الدين شيئاً، فلشريكه أن يضمنه الدين إن شاء؛ لأنه أي الشريك المشتري صار قابضاً حقه بالمقاصة، ولا ضرر عليه في تضمين ربع الدين؛ مبنى البيع على المماكسة أي المنازعة في البيع وتنقيص الثمن، فلو ضمنه ربع الدين لا يلزمه بذلك ضرر، بخلاف ما مر من صورة الصلح إذا صالح أحد الشريكين عن نصيبه على ثوب، حيث لا يضمنه الشريك الآخر ربع الدين؛ لأن مبناه على الإغماض والحطيطة، فلو ألزمناه دفع ربع الدين يتضرر بذلك، فيتخير القابض، إن شاء ضمن ربع الدين أو لا، ولا سبيل للشريك على الثوب في البيع؛ لأنه ملكه بعقده، وللشريك أن يتبع الغريم في جميع ما ذكرنا من صورة الصلح على ثوب، وصورة أخذ الدين من الدراهم والدنانير، وصورة شراء السلعة؛ لأن حقه في ذمته باق؛ لأن القابض استوفى نصيبه حقيقة لكن له حق المشاركة، فله أن لا يشاركه.
وإن اتفقا على الشركة في الثوب جاز، ولو سلم الشريك الغير القابض للقابض ما ،قبض، ثم هلك ما على الغريم بأن مات مفلساً، له أن يشارك القابض؛ لأنه إنما رضي بالتسليم ليسلم له ما في ذمة الغريم و لم يسلم، لا يقال: قسمة الدين قبل القبض لا تتصور، فكيف تتصور المقاصة فيه؛ لأنا نقول: قسمة الدين قبل القبض تجوز ضمناً، وإنما لا تجوز
قصداً، وهنا وقعت القسمة في ضمن صحة الشراء وصحة المصالحة. (ملتقط من العيني والهداية والفتح وغيرها) وبطل إلخ : قال في "الفتح": ويرد عليه أن تعبيره بالبطلان مخالف لما في "الدرر والتنوير" من قوله: صالح أحد ربي السلم عن نصيبه على ما دفع، فإن أجازه الآخر نفذ عليهما وإن رده رد، وسيأتي في كلام الشارح ملا مسكين أيضاً التصريح بالتوقف، حيث قال: فالحاصل أنه يتوقف هذا الصلح إلخ، قلت: أراد بالباطل ما قابل النافذ فيصدق بالموقوف حينئذ، بقي أن يقال : معنى الصلح على ما دفع هو أن يأخذ رأس ماله، ويفسخ عقد الشركة، وسماه صلحاً مجازاً؛ إذ هو فسخ في الحقيقة كذا في "عربي زاده".
وبطل صلح إلخ أي رجلان أسلما إلى رجل في طعام، ثم صالح أحدهما من نصيبه على رأس المال، لم يجز وعند أبي يوسف: يجوز، فالحاصل أنه يتوقف هذا الصلح عندهما على إجازة صاحبه، فإن رده بطل أصلاً،
ويكون الطعام المسلم فيه بينهما، وإن أجاز نفذ عليهما، فكأنهما صالحاه، فيكون نصف رأس المال بينهما،
Book of Compromise. Chapter: Joint Debt. A debt between two persons: one of them settles his share for a garment, then his partner has the option to either pursue the debtor for half of it (the debt) or take half of the garment from his partner, unless he guarantees a quarter of the debt. And if he receives his share, the partner shares in it, and they both pursue the debtor for the remainder.

Chapter: This chapter is about joint debt, which arises from a single cause, such as if they jointly sold a slave in one transaction, or a person destroyed it, or the debt is an inheritance among heirs. (Miskin) 'A debt between them etc.' [He delayed the joint debt from the singular because the dual comes after the singular. (Fath)] i.e. a debt shared between two partners. Joint debt is an obligation due from a single cause, like the price of a sale, the value of a jointly owned destroyed item, a loan repayment from jointly owned property, and an inheritance between two. One of them settles his share of the debt for a garment. Then his partner has the choice: if he wishes, he can pursue the debtor for half of it (i.e. half the debt) because his share remains in the debtor's liability, or he can take half the garment from his partner because he has a right of participation, as it is a substitute for his debt. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq 2/237]
'Unless he guarantees etc.': In some versions: 'he guarantees it', i.e. the partner who settled guarantees a quarter of the debt because his right is in the debt, not in the garment. There is no difference whether the settlement is by acknowledgment, silence, or denial. Then there are two further conditions: First, the settled matter must be a debt, because if the settlement was over a jointly owned specific asset, the settling partner exclusively gets the settlement substitute, and his partner has no right to participate in it because it is a complete exchange transaction. Second, the settlement compromise must be for a garment, meaning something of a different genus than the debt, because if he settled for the same genus, the partner would participate, and both would pursue the debtor. The recipient has no option as it is akin to receiving part of the debt. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq 2/237]
'And if he receives his share etc.': i.e. if one partner receives his share, the other partner joins him in it. (Miskin) And it is said in al-Fath: because division of a debt is inconceivable, and what is received is a substitute for it, so the other has the right to participate in it because it is in some sense the very object of his right, unlike if he bought a garment with it, where he does not participate because it is a complete exchange. He only had the right to participate in the garment in the section on settlement to avoid harm to the settling partner. If he hands over what was received and chooses to pursue the debtor, then the debtor dies, he may claim from the recipient half of what he received because the delivery is conditional on the safety of the remainder. But he cannot claim the very same dirhams received because his right in them fell by delivery; it does not return due to loss; it returns to the liability for a similar amount. This is from al-Zayla'i, and from this one learns the error in al-Ayni. Fath al-Mu'in: 'And they both pursue etc.': i.e. the two partners pursue the debtor for the remainder of the debt because division of a debt is inconceivable in the liability before receipt, and receipt is a substitute for it, so he may participate if he wishes because it is his right in essence.

[PAGE_086]
Book of Compromise. Joint Debt. And if he buys something with his share, he guarantees a quarter of the debt. And the settlement of one of the two parties to a salam contract from his share is invalid.

i.e. one of them. The purchasing partner guarantees.
One of the two partners in salam.
In a way, and if he wishes, he may pursue the debtor (the one liable) because his right is against him in reality. He only had the right to participate in the surplus of the garment in the section on settlement to avoid harm to the settling partner. Here, harm is absent, so he seeks a quarter of the debt. Then both pursue the debtor because they are equal in claiming. And if he hands over what was received and chooses to pursue the debtor, then his share is lost, e.g. the debtor dies insolvent, he may claim from the recipient half of what he received because the delivery is conditional on the safety of the remainder for him. If it is not safe, he may claim from him as in the case of hawala. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq 2/237]
Because
quarter
'And if he buys etc.': i.e. if one of the two partners buys something from the debtor with his share of the debt, then his partner may guarantee the debt if he wishes because the purchasing partner has effectively taken his right by set-off, and there is no harm to him in guaranteeing a quarter of the debt. The basis of sale is bargaining, so if he guarantees a quarter, no harm befalls him. Unlike the previous case of settlement where one partner settles his share for a garment, where the other partner does not guarantee a quarter of the debt because its basis is leniency and reduction; if we forced him to pay a quarter, he would be harmed. So the recipient has the option: if he wishes, he guarantees a quarter or not. The partner has no claim on the garment in sale because it is owned by the buyer through his contract. The partner may pursue the debtor in all the cases mentioned: the case of settlement for a garment, the case of taking the debt in dirhams/dinars, and the case of purchasing a commodity, because his right remains in the debtor's liability; the recipient has indeed collected his share in reality but has a right of participation, so he may choose not to participate.

If they agree on partnership in the garment, it is permissible. If the non-receiving partner delivers to the receiving partner what he received, then what is with the debtor is lost, e.g. he dies insolvent, he may participate with the recipient because he only agreed to delivery so that what is in the debtor's liability would be safe, and it is not safe. It cannot be said: division of debt before receipt is inconceivable, so how can set-off be conceived? We say: division of debt before receipt is valid indirectly, and it is invalid directly. Here division occurs within the validity of the purchase and the validity of the settlement. (Compiled from al-Ayni, al-Hidayah, al-Fath, and others.)
'And the settlement is invalid etc.': It is said in al-Fath: there is an objection that his expression 'invalid' contradicts what is in al-Durar wa al-Tanwir: 'One of the two parties to a salam contract settles his share for what was paid. If the other permits it, it is effective upon them; if he rejects, it is rejected.' And later in the commentary of Mulla Miskin, there is an explicit statement of suspension: 'The summary is that this settlement is suspended.' I say: by 'invalid' he means what is not effective; it applies to the suspended at that time. It remains to be said: the meaning of settlement for what was paid is that he takes his capital and rescinds the partnership contract; it is metaphorically called settlement, but in reality it is rescission. This is from Arabi Zadah.
'And the settlement is invalid etc.': i.e., two men gave salam to a man for food. Then one of them settled his share for the capital. It is not permissible. According to Abu Yusuf, it is permissible. The summary is that this settlement is suspended according to them (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) pending the partner's permission. If he rejects, it is completely invalid, and the food subject to salam remains between them. If he permits, it is effective upon them, as if both settled, and half the capital is between them.
Source pages p. 85

Commentary
This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq (with commentary from various sources like Ramz al-Haqa'iq, Fath, etc.) explains the rulings for joint debt (dayn mushtarak) when one partner (the settling partner) compromises his share of the debt for a specific item (like a garment). The passage is a ruling with proof, specifically using rational reasoning (istihsan and qiyas) to distinguish between various scenarios.

The passage opens by defining joint debt: it is a debt arising from a single cause, such as a joint sale, a destroyed jointly-owned item, a loan on joint capital, or an inheritance. The key point: the debt is owed by a debtor to two partners.

If one partner (the musalih) settles his share for a garment, the other partner (his sharik) has two options: (1) pursue the debtor for his half of the debt, because his share remains in the debtor's liability; or (2) take half of the garment from the settling partner, because the garment is a substitute for the debt, and he has a right to participate. However, if the other partner guarantees a quarter of the debt (i.e., takes responsibility for that portion), then he cannot take half the garment; this is because his right is in the debt itself, not the garment. The text notes there is no difference whether the settlement was by acknowledgment, silence, or denial.

Two conditions are highlighted: (a) the settled matter must be a debt, not a specific asset; if it were a specific joint asset, the settlement would be a full exchange, and no participation is allowed. (b) The settlement must be for an item of a different genus than the debt; if it's the same genus, the partner participates and both pursue the debtor.

If the partner receives his share (cash), the other partner may still participate in what was received because division of a debt before receipt is not valid; the receipt is a substitute. But if the settling partner had bought a garment with the cash, the other partner cannot participate because that's a full exchange. The participation rule in the settlement scenario is to prevent harm to the settling partner.

If the non-receiving partner chooses to pursue the debtor and hand over the received cash to the settling partner, but then the debtor dies insolvent, he can claim back half of what he handed over because delivery was conditional on safety. However, he cannot claim the specific cash because his right in it fell; it becomes a debt in the liability.

The text then discusses a second scenario: if one partner buys something from the debtor with his share of the debt (i.e., set-off), then the other partner may guarantee a quarter of the debt (i.e., demand the buying partner pay him a quarter) because sale is based on bargaining, so no harm. Unlike the settlement scenario where the basis is leniency, imposing a quarter guarantee would cause harm. So in settlement, the other partner has an option: take half the garment or guarantee quarter.

If both partners agree to share the garment, it's allowed. If the non-receiving partner hands over his share to the other and then the debtor defaults, he can still participate because his consent was contingent on safety.

Finally, the passage addresses a dispute about a salam contract: two people give salam (advance payment) for food. One of them settles his share for the capital (i.e., takes his money back). According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani, this settlement is suspended (not invalid outright but pending the other's permission). If the other rejects, it's void; if he accepts, it's effective. Abu Yusuf allows it outright. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is the suspension view, as per later authorities.

Key Terms
الدين المشترك (al-dayn al-mushtarak): A debt owed jointly to two or more persons arising from a single cause, e.g., price of a joint sale, compensation for a destroyed joint property, or an inheritance.
صلح (sulh): A compromise or settlement where one party accepts a substitute for his right, often less than the full amount, to avoid litigation.
مصالح (musalih): The partner who settles his share of the joint debt with the debtor.
رب السلم (rabb al-salam): One of the two parties who give salam (advance payment) for a commodity; they are the buyers in a salam contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a joint debt scenario where one partner settles his share for a garment, what is the default option for the other partner?
A) He must take half the garment from the settling partner.
B) He may choose to either pursue the debtor for his half of the debt OR take half the garment from the settling partner.
C) He must pursue the debtor only.
D) He automatically shares in the garment with the settling partner.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, a joint debt cannot be divided before receipt; therefore, when one partner settles for a specific item, the other partner retains a right to participate in that item to prevent harm, unless the settlement is based on a complete exchange.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
8 min
Partner Buying Goods with Share of Salam Debt
Ruling on partner's liability when one buys goods

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when a partner in a salam contract buys goods with his share of the debt and distinguish when the other partner may claim a quarter of the debt based on the nature of the transaction.

Core Idea
Sale's bargaining basis allows claiming a quarter; compromise's leniency forbids it.

This passage from the Hidayah tradition presents a nuanced ruling on the rights of partners in a salam contract. It distinguishes between two situations: one where a partner compromises his share for a garment, and another where he buys goods with his share. The ruling hinges on the nature of the transaction – sale versus compromise – and the concept of hardship (darar). The student will learn to identify when a partner can claim a quarter of the debt from the buying partner and when he cannot.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and parties
Two partners have a joint debt from a salam contract. One partner buys a commodity from the debtor using his share of the debt. Identify the parties: the buyer (qabid) and the other partner.
The purchase is with his share, meaning he uses the debt owed to him as payment.
2
State the ruling
The other partner has the right to claim a quarter (ربع الدين) of the debt from the buying partner. This is an option, not an obligation.
The text says 'ضمنه ربع الدين' – he guarantees a quarter, meaning he becomes liable if the partner chooses to claim.
3
Understand the proof via analogy
Compare with the earlier case of compromise (sulh) where one partner settles his share for a garment. There, the other partner cannot claim a quarter. The difference is the basis: sale is built on bargaining (مماكسة), while compromise is built on leniency (إغماض). In sale, claiming a quarter causes no hardship; in compromise, it would cause hardship (ضرر).
This is a qiyas with illa extracted as the nature of the transaction.
4
Apply the distinction
Given a scenario, determine whether the transaction is a sale or a compromise. If it is a sale (e.g., buying goods), the partner may claim a quarter. If it is a compromise (e.g., accepting a garment in settlement), he may not.
The key is the presence of bargaining vs. leniency.
5
Explore ancillary options
The partner may instead pursue the original debtor. If the non-buying partner later agrees to the buyer's possession and the debtor becomes insolvent, he can recover half from the buyer, analogized to hawala.
The surrender was conditional on the debtor's solvency.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو اشترى بنصيبه شيئا، ضمنه ربع الدين. أي أحدهما ضمن الشريك المشتري أحد الشريكين في السلم من وجه وإن شاء رجع على الغريم وهو المديون؛ لأن حقه عليه في الحقيقة، وإنما كان له أن يشاركه في فضل الثوب في فصل الصلح؛ كي لا يلزم المصالح الضرر ، وههنا انتفى الضرر فيرجع بربع الدين، ثم يرجعان على الغريم؛ لاستوائهما في الاقتضاء، ولو سلم له المقبوض واختار متابعة الغريم ثم توى نصيبه بأن مات الغريم مفلساً، رجع على القابض بنصف ما قبض؛ لأن التسليم مقيد بشرط سلامة الباقي له، فإذا لم يسلم له رجع عليه كما في الحوالة. لأن ربع. ولو اشترى إلخ أي لو اشترى أحد الشريكين من الذي عليه الدين بنصيبه من الدين شيئاً، فلشريكه أن يضمنه الدين إن شاء؛ لأنه أي الشريك المشتري صار قابضاً حقه بالمقاصة، ولا ضرر عليه في تضمين ربع الدين؛ مبنى البيع على المماكسة أي المنازعة في البيع وتنقيص الثمن، فلو ضمنه ربع الدين لا يلزمه بذلك ضرر، بخلاف ما مر من صورة الصلح إذا صالح أحد الشريكين عن نصيبه على ثوب، حيث لا يضمنه الشريك الآخر ربع الدين؛ لأن مبناه على الإغماض والحطيطة، فلو ألزمناه دفع ربع الدين يتضرر بذلك، فيتخير القابض، إن شاء ضمن ربع الدين أو لا، ولا سبيل للشريك على الثوب في البيع؛ لأنه ملكه بعقده، وللشريك أن يتبع الغريم في جميع ما ذكرنا من صورة الصلح على ثوب، وصورة أخذ الدين من الدراهم والدنانير، وصورة شراء السلعة؛ لأن حقه في ذمته باق؛ لأن القابض استوفى نصيبه حقيقة لكن له حق المشاركة، فله أن لا يشاركه. وإن اتفقا على الشركة في الثوب جاز، ولو سلم الشريك الغير القابض للقابض ما قبض، ثم هلك ما على الغريم بأن مات مفلساً، له أن يشارك القابض؛ لأنه إنما رضي بالتسليم ليسلم له ما في ذمة الغريم و لم يسلم، لا يقال: قسمة الدين قبل القبض لا تتصور، فكيف تتصور المقاصة فيه؛ لأنا نقول: قسمة الدين قبل القبض تجوز ضمناً، وإنما لا تجوز قصداً، وهنا وقعت القسمة في ضمن صحة الشراء وصحة المصالحة. (ملتقط من العيني والهداية والفتح وغيرها)
And if one of them buys something with his share, he guarantees a quarter of the debt. That is, one of the two partners in salam guarantees the purchasing partner from one aspect, and if he wishes, he can recourse against the debtor; because his right is really against him. He merely had the right to share in the surplus of the garment in the case of compromise, so that no hardship befalls the compromiser. Here hardship is absent, so he recovers a quarter of the debt, then both recourse against the debtor because they are equal in claim. And if the recipient surrenders what he received and chooses to pursue the debtor, then his share is lost (e.g., the debtor dies insolvent), he may recover from the recipient half of what he received; because the surrender was conditional upon the safety of the remainder for him, so if it is not safe, he may recover from him as in the case of hawala. Because a quarter... And if he buys etc.: that is, if one of the two partners buys something from the debtor with his share of the debt, his partner may, if he wishes, claim the debt from him; because the purchasing partner has taken his right by way of set-off, and there is no harm to him in claiming a quarter of the debt; the basis of sale is bargaining (i.e., dispute and price reduction), so if he claims a quarter of the debt, no harm befalls him, contrary to the earlier case of compromise when one partner compromises his share for a garment, where the other partner cannot claim a quarter of the debt; because its basis is leniency and remission, so if we obliged him to pay a quarter of the debt he would suffer. Thus the recipient chooses: if he wishes, he claims a quarter of the debt or not. The partner has no recourse to the garment in a sale because it is his property by his contract. The partner may pursue the debtor in all we mentioned: the case of compromise for a garment, the case of taking the debt in dirhams and dinars, and the case of buying a commodity; because his right remains in the debtor's liability; for the recipient has actually received his share but the partner has a right of participation, so he may choose not to participate. And if they agree on partnership in the garment, it is permissible. And if the non-receiving partner surrenders to the receiving partner what he received, then what is owed by the debtor perishes (e.g., he dies insolvent), he may join the receiving partner; because he only agreed to the surrender so that what is in the debtor's liability would be safe for him, and it is not safe. It cannot be said: division of debt before possession is inconceivable, so how can set-off be conceived? Because we say: division of debt before possession is permissible implicitly, though not explicitly. Here the division occurred within the validity of the purchase and the validity of the compromise. (Compiled from al-Ayni, al-Hidayah, al-Fath, etc.)
Source pages p. 86

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling on joint debts in a salam (forward sale) contract. The ruling is that if one of two partners in a salam buys a commodity with his share of the debt, his partner has the option to claim a quarter of the debt from him. The commentary explains the reasoning: the purchasing partner has effectively taken his share by set-off (muqassa), and because the basis of sale is bargaining, forcing the purchasing partner to pay a quarter causes no hardship. This contrasts with the earlier case of compromise (sulh) where one partner settles his share for a garment; there, the other partner cannot claim a quarter because the basis of compromise is leniency, and forcing payment would cause hardship. The passage further discusses the partner's options: he can either claim a quarter from the buyer or pursue the original debtor. If the non-receiving partner later agrees to the buyer's possession and then the debtor becomes insolvent, he can recover from the buyer half of what he received, analogized to hawala (transfer of debt). Finally, the passage addresses a potential objection about dividing a debt before possession, explaining that such division is valid implicitly when it occurs within a valid transaction.

Key Terms
رب السلم (rabb al-salam): The party who advances payment in a salam contract.
ضمان (daman): Liability to pay; the partner becomes liable for a quarter of the debt.
مقاصة (muqassa): Set-off; the buyer takes his share by offsetting his debt.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a salam partnership, one partner buys goods with his share of the debt. The other partner can claim what fraction from the buyer?
A) Half the debt
B) A quarter of the debt
C) The entire debt
D) Nothing

Key Takeaway
The partner may claim a quarter of the debt from the buyer because sale's bargaining basis avoids hardship, unlike compromise where leniency prevents such a claim.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute: One Partner's Settlement for Capital in Salam
Intra-Hanafi dispute on salam partner's settlement

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi intra-madhhab disagreement regarding a salam partner's settlement for the capital and identify the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
A salam partner's settlement for capital is suspended pending the other's ratification; direct validity would require impermissible debt division.

This lesson examines a critical disagreement among the Hanafi imams concerning a partnership in a salam contract. When one partner attempts to settle his share for the capital amount he paid, is the settlement valid immediately or does it require the other partner's consent? The matn declares it invalid, but later commentaries reveal a nuanced suspension. We will walk through the positions of Abu Hanifa, Muhammad, and Abu Yusuf, and understand the practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi majority position
Identify the ruling of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani as presented in the matn and commentary: the settlement is invalid (batal) in the sense of being suspended (mawquf) pending the other partner's ratification.
The matn's 'batal' is interpreted as 'not immediately effective'.
2
Identify the opposing view (Abu Yusuf)
State Abu Yusuf's position: the settlement is valid for the one who performs it, without requiring the other's consent, based on analogy to other joint debts.
Abu Yusuf considers it a joint debt where a partner may settle his share.
3
Follow the majority's proof
Analyze the reasoning: the settlement, if valid, would either apply to his share alone (necessitating division of the debt before possession – invalid) or to half of both shares (dissolving the other's contract without consent – also invalid). Hence it must be suspended.
The key point is that the salam debt is not yet in possession, so division before possession is prohibited.
4
Analyze Abu Yusuf's response
Abu Yusuf analogizes to ordinary joint debts where a partner can settle his portion. The majority respond that the analogy fails because salam involves a debt of specific goods not yet in hand.
The distinction rests on the unique nature of salam: the subject matter is a debt (dayn) of fungible goods, not a tangible asset.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf and mufta bihi
The practical difference: under the majority, if the other partner rejects, the settlement is void and goods remain shared; under Abu Yusuf, the settlement stands and the other partner has options. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf within the school; the mufta bihi is the majority view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبطل صلح أحد ربي السلم من نصيبه على ما دفع. [بطل إلخ] : قال في الفتح: ويرد عليه أن تعبيره بالبطلان مخالف لما في الدرر والتنوير من قوله: صالح أحد ربي السلم عن نصيبه على ما دفع، فإن أجازه الآخر نفذ عليهما وإن رده رد، وسيأتي في كلام الشارح ملا مسكين أيضاً التصريح بالتوقف، حيث قال: فالحاصل أنه يتوقف هذا الصلح إلخ، قلت: أراد بالباطل ما قابل النافذ فيصدق بالموقوف حينئذ، بقي أن يقال : معنى الصلح على ما دفع هو أن يأخذ رأس ماله، ويفسخ عقد الشركة، وسماه صلحاً مجازاً؛ إذ هو فسخ في الحقيقة كذا في عربي زاده. وبطل صلح إلخ أي رجلان أسلما إلى رجل في طعام، ثم صالح أحدهما من نصيبه على رأس المال، لم يجز وعند أبي يوسف: يجوز، فالحاصل أنه يتوقف هذا الصلح عندهما على إجازة صاحبه، فإن رده بطل أصلاً، عندهما، ويكون الطعام المسلم فيه بينهما، وإن أجاز نفذ عليهما، فكأنهما صالحاه، فيكون نصف رأس المال بينهما، ونصف الطعام المسلم فيه أيضاً بينهما، وعنده: الصلح جائز على من باشره، وله نصف رأس المال، وشريكه إن شاء شاركه فيما قبض، ثم يتبعان المطلوب بنصف الطعام المسلم فيه وإن شاء سلم له ما قبض ويتبع المسلم إليه بنصف المسلم فيه إلا إذا توى ما على المسلم إليه فليرجع على الشريك المصالح، ثم المصالح بالخيار إن شاء دفع إليه نصف ما قبض، وإن شاء دفع إليه ربع المسلم فيه. (ملا مسكين) على ما دفع أي بطل صلح أحد ربي السلم إذا صالح من نصيبه على ما دفع من رأس المال، وهذا عندهما، وعند أبي يوسف: يجوز؛ لأنه دين مشترك، فإذا صالح أحدهما على حصته جاز، كما في سائر الديون، ولهما: أنه لو جاز، فإما أن يجوزه في نصيبه خاصةً، أو في النصف من النصيبين، فعلى الأول يلزم قسمة الدين قبل القبض؛ لأن خصوصية نصيبه لا تظهر إلا بالتميز ولا تمييز إلا بالقسمة، وقد تقدم بطلانها، وإن كان الثاني، فلابد من إجازة الآخر؛ لأنه فسخ على شريكه عقده فيفتقر إلى رضاه. واعلم أن الخلاف ثابت على الصحيح سواء خلطا رأس المال أو لا، وقيل: إن لم يخلطا رأس المال جاز عندهما أيضاً، وإنما قيد بقوله: على ما دفع؛ لأنه لو كان على غيره لا يجوز بالإجماع؛ لما فيه من الاستبدال بالمسلم فيه. (فتح، عيني)
And the compromise of one of the two masters of salam from his share for what he paid is invalid. [It is invalid etc.]: He said in al-Fath: It is objected that his expression of invalidity contradicts what is in al-Durar and al-Tanwir, where it is said: If one of the two masters of salam compromises his share for what was paid, and the other ratifies it, it becomes binding on both; if he rejects it, it is rejected. And in the commentary of Mulla Miskeen there is also explicit mention of suspension, where he said: So the result is that this compromise is suspended, etc. I say: He meant by 'invalid' what is opposite of 'effective', so it applies to the suspended at that time. It remains to be said: The meaning of compromise for what was paid is that he takes his capital and dissolves the partnership contract; it is called compromise metaphorically, for it is actually a dissolution, as in 'Arabi Zada. And the compromise is invalid etc.: i.e., two men give salam to a man for food, then one of them compromises his share for the capital; it is not permissible. According to Abu Yusuf: it is permissible. So the result is that this compromise is suspended according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) pending the ratification of his partner; if he rejects it, it is invalid absolutely according to them, and the salam food is between them; and if he ratifies it, it is binding on both, so it is as if both compromised, and half of the capital is between them, and half of the salam food is also between them. According to him (Abu Yusuf): the compromise is valid for the one who performed it, and he gets half the capital, and his partner may, if he wishes, participate in what he received, and then they both pursue the debtor for half the salam food; or if he wishes, he surrenders what he received and pursues the Muslim ilayh (the seller) for half the salam food; except if what was due from the Muslim ilayh is lost, then he recovers from the compromising partner; then the compromising partner has the choice: either he pays him half of what he received, or he pays him a quarter of the salam food. (Mulla Miskeen) For what was paid: i.e., the compromise of one of the two masters of salam is invalid if he compromises his share for what he paid of the capital. This is according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad). According to Abu Yusuf: it is permissible, because it is a joint debt; if one compromises his share, it is permissible, as in other debts. According to the two: if it were permissible, then either it is permissible in his particular share alone, or in half of the two shares. On the first, it necessitates division of debt before possession, because the specificity of his share is not apparent except by distinction, and distinction is only through division, and its invalidity has preceded. If the second, then the other's ratification is necessary, because it is a dissolution of his partner's contract, so it requires his consent. Know that the disagreement exists on the correct position regardless of whether they mixed the capital or not. And it is said: if they did not mix the capital, it is permissible according to both as well. And it is restricted by his saying 'for what was paid' because if it were for something else, it is invalid by consensus, due to substitution of the salam goods. (Fath, Ayni)
Source pages p. 86

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning the validity of a compromise (sulh) when one of two partners in a salam contract settles his share for the capital amount he paid. According to the matn (Kanz al-Daqaiq), such a settlement is invalid (batal). The commentary from al-Fath notes a nuance: the term 'invalid' here means 'not immediately effective' or 'suspended' (mawquf), pending the other partner's ratification. The dispute: Abu Hanifa and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) hold that the settlement is suspended on the other partner's consent; if he rejects it, the settlement is void, and the goods remain jointly owned. Abu Yusuf, however, allows the settlement outright for the one who performed it, with the other partner having options to participate or not. The reasoning of the majority (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) is that the settlement necessarily involves either a division of the debt before possession (which is invalid) or a dissolution of the partnership contract requiring the other's consent. Abu Yusuf analogizes it to other joint debts where a partner can settle his share. The passage also clarifies that the disagreement holds whether the capital was mixed or not, and restricts the ruling to settlements for the capital amount.

Key Terms
صلح (sulh): A settlement where one partner gives up his share of the salam goods in exchange for the capital he paid.
رب السلم (rabb al-salam): A party who advances payment in a salam contract; both parties are co-owners of the debt until delivery.
إجازة (ijaza): Ratification or consent by the other partner to make the settlement effective.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, what is the status of a settlement by one salam partner for the capital amount without the other partner's explicit consent?
A) It is fully valid and binding on both.
B) It is absolutely void with no possibility of validation.
C) It is suspended pending the other partner's ratification.
D) It is valid for the settling partner only.

Key Takeaway
The settlement of one salam partner for the capital is suspended (not absolutely void) and requires the other partner's ratification to become effective; this is the mufta bihi position.

Compromise by a Salam Partner: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on validity of salam partner's compromise for capital

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi disagreement on a salam partner's compromise for capital and state the mufta bihi position with its supporting proof.

Core Idea
A salam partner's compromise for capital is invalid because it requires either prohibited debt division or partner consent.

When two parties jointly advance capital in a salam (forward sale) contract, one may wish to compromise his share for the original capital. Is that valid? This lesson explores the disagreement between Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad (invalid) and Imam Abu Yusuf (valid). We will analyze the proofs and identify the relied-upon position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the dispute
Precisely what is being ruled upon: one salam partner (rabb al-salam) compromises his share of the debt owed by the seller for the capital he originally paid. The dispute is whether this compromise is valid.
The debt is held in common (dayn mushtarak) by the two partners.
2
State the two positions
Abu Hanifa and Muhammad hold it is invalid (batil). Abu Yusuf holds it is valid (ja'iz). State each clearly.
The matn indicates 'عندهما' refers to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad.
3
Follow Abu Yusuf's proof
Abu Yusuf analogizes this to any shared debt: since the debt is common, each partner may compromise his own share independently, just as in other debts.
He uses qiyas on general shared debts.
4
Analyze the counter-proof of the two
The two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) reject the analogy. They argue that if the compromise were valid, it would have to be either: (1) only on his specific share, which requires dividing the debt before receipt (batil), or (2) on half of the total debt, which requires the other partner's consent (since it rescinds part of the contract). Neither condition is met.
Division of debt before receipt is prohibited in salam because it leads to uncertainty (gharar) and is considered invalid per earlier fiqh principles.
5
Determine the mufta bihi and note the tarjih
The relied-upon position is the invalidity declared by Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. This is recorded in Zahir al-Riwayah and upheld by later authorities like al-Marghinani and al-Ayni.
The rule applies whether or not the capital was mixed, though some say mixing may change the ruling; the correct view is that mixing is irrelevant.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
على ما دفع أي بطل صلح أحد ربي السلم إذا صالح من نصيبه على ما دفع من رأس المال، وهذا عندهما، وعند أبي يوسف: يجوز؛ لأنه دين مشترك، فإذا صالح أحدهما على حصته جاز، كما في سائر الديون، ولهما: أنه لو جاز، فإما أن يجوزه في نصيبه خاصةً، أو في النصف من النصيبين، فعلى الأول يلزم قسمة الدين قبل القبض؛ لأن خصوصية نصيبه لا تظهر إلا بالتميز ولا تمييز إلا بالقسمة، وقد تقدم بطلانها، وإن كان الثاني، فلابد من إجازة الآخر؛ لأنه فسخ على شريكه عقده فيفتقر إلى رضاه. واعلم أن الخلاف ثابت على الصحيح سواء خلطا رأس المال أو لا، وقيل: إن لم يخلطا رأس المال جاز عندهما أيضاً، وإنما قيد بقوله: "على ما دفع"؛ لأنه لو كان على غيره لا يجوز بالإجماع؛ لما فيه من الاستبدال بالمسلم فيه. (فتح، عيني)
On what was paid: meaning the compromise of one of the two parties to a salam contract if he compromises his share for what was paid of the capital is invalid. This is according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), and according to Abu Yusuf it is permissible because it is a shared debt, so if one of them compromises his share it is permissible, as in other debts. The two argue: if it were permissible, then either it is permitted only in his share specifically, or in half of the two shares. On the first, it entails division of a debt before receipt, because specificity of his share does not appear except by distinction, and there is no distinction except by division, and its invalidity has preceded. On the second, the other's permission is necessary because it is a rescission of his contract with his partner, so it requires his consent. Know that the disagreement is established correctly whether they mixed the capital or not, and it is said: if they did not mix the capital, it is permissible according to the two. The restriction to "on what was paid" is because if it were on other than that, it would be invalid by consensus, due to substitution of the salam commodity. (Fath, Ayni)
Source pages p. 87

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling on a compromise (sulh) by one of two parties in a salam contract. The matn states that if one partner compromises his share for the capital he paid, the compromise is invalid according to Imam Muhammad (and by extension Abu Hanifa according to the text). Abu Yusuf disagrees, citing that the debt is shared and compromising one's share is akin to compromising any other shared debt. The two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) counter: if it were valid, it would either apply to his share alone (which requires division of the debt before receipt, which is invalid) or to half of both shares (which requires the other partner's consent, as it rescinds part of the contract). The text clarifies that the disagreement holds regardless of whether the capital was mixed, though some say mixing changes the ruling. The condition "on what was paid" is crucial; compromising for anything else would be invalid by consensus, as it substitutes the salam commodity.

Key Terms
ربي السلم (rabbā al-salam): The party who advances capital in a salam contract (forward sale).
صلح (ṣulḥ): A compromise agreement to settle a dispute, here used as a transaction to exit from a shared debt.
دين مشترك (dayn mushtarak): A debt owed to two or more creditors collectively in undivided shares.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Valid, because it is a shared debt

C) Valid, only if the capital was not mixed
D) Invalid only if the capital was mixed

Key Takeaway
A salam partner's compromise for capital is invalid in the Hanafi school because it cannot be executed without either prohibited debt division or the partner's consent.
