Conditions for Valid Compromise with Mixed Assets and Currency Payment
Ruling on validity of compromise when estate has gold, silver, and other assets.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three conditions required for a valid compromise when an heir is given gold or silver from an estate containing mixed assets, and explain why each condition prevents riba.

Core Idea
A compromise giving gold or silver from a mixed estate is invalid unless the heir receives more than his share of that currency to avoid riba.

When an estate contains gold, silver, and other assets like goods or real estate, the heirs might agree to give one heir gold or silver as his entire share. This transaction is treated as a compensation (mu'awadah), not a release (ibra'), because releasing tangible property is invalid. Since it is a compensation, the rules of sale apply, particularly the prohibition of riba. This lesson explains the conditions that must be met for such a compromise to be valid, focusing on the amount given and the requirement of hand-to-hand exchange.

Guided Path
1
Identify the transaction type
Determine whether the compromise is a release (ibra') or a compensation (mu'awadah). The text explains that ibra' applies only to debts, not tangibles, so this compromise is a mu'awadah (like a sale).
This classification triggers the conditions of sale, including riba rules.
2
State the core condition for validity
The heir must receive more of the given currency than his share of that currency in the estate. This excess compensates him for his share of the other assets (goods, real estate).
If he gets equal or less, part of the consideration is without compensation, which is riba.
3
Check the hand-to-hand exchange requirement
For the portion of gold or silver given in exchange for his share of the same currency, immediate delivery (qabd) in the session is required because it is a currency exchange (sarf).
This applies only to that portion; the rest (for non-currency assets) is like a sale of goods for currency.
4
Recognize invalid scenarios
If the heir receives less than or equal to his share of the currency, or if his share of the currency is unknown, the compromise is invalid due to certainty or probability of riba.
Unknown share leads to potential inequality, so it is invalid as a precaution.
5
Contrast with payment in goods
If the heirs give the heir goods (urud) instead of gold or silver, the compromise is valid unconditionally because there is no riba in goods.
Riba rules apply only to gold, silver, and certain food items in Hanafi fiqh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وعن نقدين وغيرهما بأحد النقدين لا ما لم يكن المعطى أكثر من حظه منه، ولو في أحد النقدين أي لا يصح الصلح بصيغة المفعول من نصيب المصالح أي من جنس المعطى بعوض التركة دين على الناس فأخرجوه ليكون الدين لهم، بطل، = أي الصلح في العين والدين فإن كان على وجه الإخبار كقوله هو بريء من مالي قبله، فهو صحيح متناول للدين والعين، فلا تسمع الدعوى، وكذا إذا قال: لا ملك لي في هذه العين ذكره في "المبسوط" و"المحيط" ، فعلم أن قوله: لا استحق قبله حقاً مطلقاً ولا استحقاقاً، ولا دعوى يمنع الدعوى بحق من الحقوق قبل الإقرار عيناً كان أو ديناً، قال في "المبسوط": ويدخل في قوله: "لا حق لي قبل "فلان" كل عين أو دين وكل كفالة أو جناية أو إجارة أو حدّ، فإن ادعى الطالب بعد ذلك حقاً لم تقبل بينته عليه حتى يشهدوا أنه كان بعد البراءة إلخ. (فتح) وعن نقدين إلخ: أي إذا كانت التركة مشتملة على الذهب والفضة وغيرهما من العروض والعقار، فأخرجت الورثة أحدهم بأحد النقدين أي أعطوه عن نصيبه من التركة إما الذهب أو الفضة، لا يجوز هذا الصلح ما لم يكن الذي أعطوه أكثر من هذا النقد الذي دفعوه إليه؛ ليكون نصيبه بمثله، والزيادة في مقابلة حقه . التركة تحرزاً عن الربا؛ لأنه لما حمل على المعاوضة لتعذر حمله على الإبراء من الأعيان، وجب اعتبار شرط المعاوضة فيه، وذلك بما ذكرنا، وإنما تعذر الحمل على الإبراء؛ لأن الإسقاط إنما يستعمل في الديون لا في الأعيان، ولابد من التقابض في المجلس فيما يقابل من نصيبه من الذهب والفضة؛ لأنه صرف في هذا القدر، ولو كان ما أعطوه أقل أو مساوياً لنصيبه، أو لا يعلم قدر نصيبه من الدراهم، فسد الصلح. ووجه الفساد فيما إذا أعطوه قدر حقه أو أقل كون العوض أي العروض وبعض الذهب أو الفضة حاصلاً بلا عوض، فيكون رباً، وكذا إذا لم يعلم قدر نصيبه؛ لاحتمال الربا؛ لأن الفساد على تقدير كونه مساوياً له أو أقل، فكان أرجح وأولى بالاعتبار، بخلاف الصحة؛ فإنها من جانب واحد، وهو ما إذا كان المأخوذ أكثر من نصيبه، فكانت العبرة لجانب الفساد؛ لكونه من وجهين، ولو كان ما أعطوه عرضاً جاز مطلقاً؛ لعدم الربا. (فتح عيني، ملا مسكين بتوضيح من المحشي)
And regarding two currencies and other things with one of the two currencies: not valid unless what is given is more than his share from it. And even if in one of the two currencies [it is not valid unless...] This means the compromise is not valid in the passive sense from the share of the compromising party, i.e., from the same genus as what is given in exchange for the estate or a debt owed by people, so they exclude him to make the debt theirs: it is invalid, meaning the compromise on both tangible and debt. But if it is in the form of information (ikhbar) like he says 'he is free from what is owed to me before him', it is valid, covering debt and tangible, and the claim is not heard. Similarly if he says 'I have no ownership in this tangible', mentioned in al-Mabsut and al-Muhit. Thus it is known that his statement 'I have no right before him absolutely, no entitlement, no claim' prevents claiming any right before the admission, whether tangible or debt. Al-Mabsut says: in his statement 'I have no right before so-and-so' includes every tangible or debt, every guarantee, crime, lease, or hadd punishment. If the claimant later claims a right, his evidence is not accepted until they witness that it was after the release etc. (Fath) And regarding two currencies etc.: meaning if the estate includes gold, silver, and other items like goods and real estate, and the heirs exclude one of them by one of the two currencies, i.e., they give him either gold or silver for his share, this compromise is not valid unless what they give him is more than his share of that currency, so that his share is equal to it, and the excess is in exchange for his right from the rest of the estate, to avoid riba. Since it is interpreted as a compensation (mu'awadah) because it cannot be interpreted as a release (ibra') from tangible items, the condition of compensation must be considered. It cannot be interpreted as release because release is only used for debts, not tangibles. Hand-to-hand exchange in the session is required for the portion corresponding to his share of gold and silver, because it is currency exchange in that amount. If what they give him is less than or equal to his share, or his share of dirhams is not known, the compromise becomes invalid. The reason for invalidity when they give him equal or less is that the consideration (i.e., the goods and some gold or silver) is obtained without compensation, thus riba. Similarly if his share is unknown, due to possibility of riba. Because invalidity on the assumption of equality or less is more probable and should be considered, unlike validity which is only on one side (when he receives more). If what they give him is goods (urud), it is valid absolutely because no riba. (Fath, Ayni, Mulla Miskin with clarification from the annotator)
Source pages p. 88

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling when the estate contains a mix of gold, silver, and other assets, and the heirs exclude one heir by giving him either gold or silver. The matn states that the compromise is not valid unless the heir receives more of that currency than his share of that currency. The commentary explains that this is because the transaction is treated as a compensation (mu'awadah) rather than a release (ibra'), since release of tangible property is invalid. Therefore, the conditions of a sale apply: to avoid riba, the heir must receive more than his share so that the excess compensates him for his share of the non-currency assets. If he receives equal or less, part of the consideration goes without compensation, which is riba. Furthermore, when gold or silver is exchanged, immediate hand-to-hand delivery is required in the session (sarf rules). If his share of dirhams is unknown, the compromise is invalid due to potential riba. If the payment is in goods (non-monetary), there is no riba, so it is valid unconditionally. The commentary also includes a digression about statements of release (ibra') and how they affect claims, citing al-Mabsut and al-Muhit.

Key Terms
نقدين (naqdayn): The two currencies: gold and silver.
معاوضة (mu'āwaḍah): Compensatory transaction (like sale), as opposed to ibra' (release).
إبراء (ibrā'): Release from a debt; not applicable to tangible property.
ربا (ribā): Usury or unlawful increase in exchange of same genus items.
صرف (ṣarf): Currency exchange; requires immediate hand-to-hand possession.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When heirs give an heir gold from an estate containing gold, silver, and other assets, what condition must be met for the compromise to be valid?
A) The gold given must be equal to his share of the gold
B) The gold given must be more than his share of the gold
C) The gold given must be less than his share of the gold
D) The gold given can be any amount if the other heirs agree

Key Takeaway
A compromise where an heir receives gold or silver from a mixed estate is only valid if he receives more than his share of that currency, with immediate hand-to-hand exchange for that portion, to prevent riba.

Invalidity of Compromise Giving an Estate Debt to an Heir
Ruling on validity of compromise when estate debt is assigned to an heir

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish when an assignment of a debt from an estate to an heir is invalid as a compromise and when it is valid as a statement of release (iqrar).

Core Idea
Assigning an estate debt to an heir in a compromise is invalid; only a release statement is valid.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq addresses a specific scenario in estate distribution: when the estate includes a debt owed by a third party, and the heirs attempt to settle by giving that debt to one heir as his share. The ruling draws a sharp line between an invalid compromise and a valid release statement. Understanding this distinction is essential for correctly applying Hanafi law to inheritance compromises involving debts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The estate has a debt receivable from a third party. The heirs exclude one heir by giving him that debt as his share of the estate.
2
State the default ruling
According to the matn, such a compromise is invalid (batal).
The ruling applies to the compromise itself, not to a mere statement.
3
Understand the reason for invalidity
The invalidity arises because the debt is transferred to a person other than the original debtor, which is akin to selling a debt to a non-debtor, a prohibited transaction in Hanafi law.
This reason is inferred from the distinction made in the commentary.
4
Distinguish the valid scenario
If the same outcome is achieved through a statement of information (ikhbar), such as saying 'he is free from what he owes me' or 'I have no claim on him', it is valid as an iqrar (admission) and bars future claims.
The form matters: a transfer is invalid; an admission is valid.
5
Appreciate the scope of iqrar
The commentary from al-Mabsut explains that such release statements cover all types of claims, including debts, tangibles, guarantees, crimes, leases, and prescribed punishments.
This breadth ensures litigation is prevented unless new evidence emerges.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو في التركة دين على الناس فأخرجوه ليكون الدين لهم، بطل، = أي الصلح في العين والدين فإن كان على وجه الإخبار كقوله هو بريء من مالي قبله، فهو صحيح متناول للدين والعين، فلا تسمع الدعوى، وكذا إذا قال: لا ملك لي في هذه العين ذكره في "المبسوط" و"المحيط" ، فعلم أن قوله: لا استحق قبله حقاً مطلقاً ولا استحقاقاً، ولا دعوى يمنع الدعوى بحق من الحقوق قبل الإقرار عيناً كان أو ديناً، قال في "المبسوط": ويدخل في قوله: "لا حق لي قبل "فلان" كل عين أو دين وكل كفالة أو جناية أو إجارة أو حدّ، فإن ادعى الطالب بعد ذلك حقاً لم تقبل بينته عليه حتى يشهدوا أنه كان بعد البراءة إلخ. (فتح)
And if in the estate there is a debt owed by people, and they (heirs) exclude him so that the debt becomes theirs, it is invalid, i.e., the compromise on both tangible property and debt. But if it is in the form of information (ikhbar) like his saying 'he is free from what he owes me before him', then it is valid, covering both debt and tangible, and the claim is not heard. Similarly if he says 'I have no ownership in this tangible', mentioned in al-Mabsut and al-Muhit. Thus it is known that his saying 'I have no right before him absolutely, no entitlement, no claim' prevents claiming any right before the admission, whether tangible or debt. Al-Mabsut says: his statement 'I have no right before so-and-so' includes every tangible or debt, every guarantee, crime, lease, or hadd punishment. If the claimant later claims a right, his evidence is not accepted until they witness that it was after the release etc. (Fath)
Source pages p. 88

Commentary
This passage covers the ruling when the estate includes a debt owed by third parties, and the heirs attempt to exclude one heir by giving him that debt (i.e., assigning the debt to him). According to the matn, such a compromise is invalid when it involves both the tangible assets and the debt. The commentary explains that the invalidity is because it would entail transferring the debt to a person other than the debtor, which is not permissible (i.e., it amounts to sale of debt to a non-debtor, which is invalid in Hanafi law). However, the passage distinguishes this from a mere statement of release or disclaimer. If the heir simply says 'he is free from what he owes me' or 'I have no claim on him', this is valid as an iqrar (admission) and prevents any future claim, regardless of whether the subject is tangible or debt. The commentary cites al-Mabsut and al-Muhit for the principle that statements like 'I have no right before him' cover all types of claims (debts, tangibles, guarantees, etc.) and bar future litigation unless new evidence shows the claim arose after the statement.

Key Terms
إقرار (iqrār): Admission or acknowledgment of a fact, here a statement of release or disclaimer.
براءة (barā'ah): Release or discharge from a claim.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because the debt is not yet due
B) Because it transfers the debt to a non-debtor
C) Because the heir must take tangible assets
D) Because the other heirs must consent

Key Takeaway
A compromise that transfers an estate debt to an heir is invalid; only a statement of release (iqrar) can validly achieve such a result.

Sulh with Two Currencies: Condition of Excess to Avoid Riba
Ruling on sulh with two currencies and condition of excess

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on sulh when the estate contains gold and silver, and apply the condition that the amount given must exceed the settlee's share to avoid riba.

Core Idea
In sulh involving currency from an estate, the given amount must exceed the share to prevent riba – equality or less invalidates.

This lesson examines a key ruling from Kitab al-Sulh regarding estates that include both gold and silver along with other goods. The Hanafi scholars set a precise condition to avoid falling into riba. We'll work through the reasoning behind requiring an excess and the consequences when the condition is not met.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The estate includes gold, silver, and other assets. The heirs make a sulh with a claimant by giving him only gold or silver for his entire share.
The settlee receives a portion of currency, not goods.
2
State the ruling
The sulh is only valid if the amount of currency given is more than the settlee's share. If it is equal or less, the sulh is invalid (fasid).
This applies to both gold and silver individually.
3
Understand the legal basis
The sulh is treated as an exchange (mu'awada) because discharge (ibra) applies only to debts, not to physical properties. Therefore, conditions of exchange apply, including avoidance of riba.
The transaction is akin to sarf (money exchange) for the currency portion, requiring hand-to-hand exchange (taqabud) and equality.
4
Analyze the riba concern
If the given amount equals or is less than the share, the deficit is compensated by the other goods in the estate without additional consideration, creating an unequal exchange that constitutes riba.
The excess (when given more) serves as compensation for the non-currency assets.
5
Note the exception
If the heirs give goods (not currency) instead, the sulh is valid unconditionally because riba is not present in non-currency exchanges.
This is because riba only concerns certain defined goods (currency and foodstuffs) per Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

فإن كان على وجه الإخبار كقوله هو بريء من مالي قبله، فهو صحيح متناول للدين والعين، فلا تسمع الدعوى، وكذا إذا قال: لا ملك لي في هذه العين ذكره في "المبسوط" و"المحيط" ، فعلم أن قوله: لا استحق قبله حقاً مطلقاً ولا استحقاقاً، ولا دعوى يمنع الدعوى بحق من الحقوق قبل الإقرار عيناً كان أو ديناً، قال في "المبسوط": ويدخل في قوله: "لا حق لي قبل "فلان" كل عين أو دين وكل كفالة أو جناية أو إجارة أو حدّ، فإن ادعى الطالب بعد ذلك حقاً لم تقبل بينته عليه حتى يشهدوا أنه كان بعد البراءة إلخ. (فتح) وعن نقدين إلخ: أي إذا كانت التركة مشتملة على الذهب والفضة وغيرهما من العروض والعقار، فأخرجت الورثة أحدهم بأحد النقدين أي أعطوه عن نصيبه من التركة إما الذهب أو الفضة، لا يجوز هذا الصلح ما لم يكن الذي أعطوه أكثر من هذا النقد الذي دفعوه إليه؛ ليكون نصيبه بمثله، والزيادة في مقابلة حقه . التركة تحرزاً عن الربا؛ لأنه لما حمل على المعاوضة لتعذر حمله على الإبراء من الأعيان، وجب اعتبار شرط المعاوضة فيه، وذلك بما ذكرنا، وإنما تعذر الحمل على الإبراء؛ لأن الإسقاط إنما يستعمل في الديون لا في الأعيان، ولابد من التقابض في المجلس فيما يقابل من نصيبه من الذهب والفضة؛ لأنه صرف في هذا القدر، ولو كان ما أعطوه أقل أو مساوياً لنصيبه، أو لا يعلم قدر نصيبه من الدراهم، فسد الصلح.

وإن شرطوا إلخ الورثة في هذه المسألة أن يبرأ الغرماء منه أي من نصيب المصالح من الدين صح الصلح. (مسكين) وقال في "الفتح": لأنه إسقاط أو تمليك للدين ممن هو عليه وهذه حيلة الجواز، وأخرى أن يعجلوا قضاء نصيبه متبرعين قال في "الهداية": وفي الوجهين ضرر لبقية الورثة، والأوجه أن يقرضوا المصالح مقدار نصيبه، ويصالحوا عما وراء الدين ويحيلهم على استيفاء نصيبه من الغرماء وليس عليهم في هذه الصورة ضرر؛ لأنه وإن خرج منهم قدر الدين لكن حصل لهم الدين بمقابلته، فانتفى الضرر عنهم إلا ضرر التقديم، فإن العين خير من الدين، وأوجه أن منه من تمر أو نحوه بقدر الدين ثم يحيلهم على الغرماء، أو يحيلهم ابتداء

[رمز الحقائق: ۲۳۸/٢]
Book of Sulh. Common debt. And regarding two currencies and other goods with one of the two currencies, it is not [valid] unless what is given is more than his share from it, and regarding one of the two currencies, i.e., the sulh is not valid in the passive form from the share of the settlee, i.e., from the kind of what is given. With compensation. The estate is a debt owed by the people, so they take it out to make the debt theirs; it is invalid. = i.e., the sulh regarding the property and debt. If it is on the basis of declaration, like his saying: he is free from any property of mine that he has, then it is valid, encompassing debt and property, and the claim is not heard. Similarly, if he says: I have no ownership in this property. It is mentioned in al-Mabsut and al-Muhit. So it is known that his saying: I have no right before him absolutely, no entitlement, and no claim, prevents the claim of any right before the acknowledgment, whether property or debt. He said in al-Mabsut: his saying 'I have no right against so-and-so' includes every property or debt, every guarantee, crime, lease, or hadd penalty. If the claimant later claims a right, his evidence is not accepted unless they testify that it was after the declaration. (Fath) And regarding two currencies etc.: i.e., if the estate includes gold and silver and other movable and immovable goods, and the heirs take out one of them with one of the two currencies, i.e., they give him for his share of the estate either gold or silver, this sulh is not valid unless what they give is more than the currency they paid to him; so that his share is equivalent to it, and the excess is in return for his right. The estate is to avoid riba; because since it is treated as a transaction (mu'awada) due to the impossibility of treating it as a discharge (ibra') from the properties, it becomes necessary to consider the condition of transaction in it, as we mentioned. And the impossibility of treating it as a discharge is because discharge is only used for debts, not for properties. And hand-to-hand exchange (taqabud) in the session is required for what corresponds to his share of gold and silver, because it is sarf in this amount. And if they gave him less than or equal to his share, or his share in dirhams is not known, the sulh is corrupt (fasid). And the explanation of the corruption when they give him the amount of his right or less is that the consideration (the goods and some gold or silver) is obtained without compensation, so it becomes riba. Similarly, if his share is not known, due to the possibility of riba. Because the corruption is based on the assumption that it is equal to or less than his share, so it is more likely and more deserving of consideration. Unlike validity, which is one-sided, i.e., when what is taken is more than his share, so the consideration is for the side of corruption because it is two-sided. And if what they gave is goods, it is permissible absolutely, due to the absence of riba. (Fath 'Ayni, Mulla Miskeen with clarification from the commentator) And regarding the estate is a debt etc.: i.e., if the estate includes a debt owed by the people, and they agree to take out the settlee from the debt to make the debt theirs, the sulh is invalid absolutely in the debt and property. It was said: this is the view of Abu Hanifa. And according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), the contract remains valid with respect to what is beyond the debt. And it was said: this is the view of all. (Miskeen) Batal: i.e., this sulh is invalid because it is a transfer of ownership of the debt which is the share of the settlee from someone else, and transferring ownership of it from someone other than the debtor is not permissible. And it is equal in this whether they specify the share of the debt or not, according to Abu Hanifa. And it should be permissible according to them (the two) regarding other than the debt if they specify his share. And the origin of the dispute is when one combines a free man and a slave, or a slaughtered sheep that is permissible and a dead one, and sells them in a single transaction, and distinguishes each of them from the price: according to him (Abu Hanifa) it is invalid in all, and according to them it is valid in the slave and the permissible sheep. [Ramz al-Haqaiq: 2/238] And if they stipulate that the debtors be discharged from it, it is valid. And if the deceased had a debt that engulfs the estate, the sulh and division are invalid. The share of the settlee from the debt was with the estate? i.e., division of debt. And if they stipulate etc.: the heirs in this issue that the debtors be discharged from it, i.e., from the share of the settlee from the debt, the sulh is valid. (Miskeen) And he said in al-Fath: because it is a discharge or a transfer of ownership of the debt to the one who owes it, and this is a legal stratagem (hila) for permissibility. Another stratagem is that they expedite payment of his share as a donation. He said in al-Hidaya: In both ways there is harm to the remaining heirs. The best is that they lend the settlee the amount of his share, and they make a sulh regarding what is beyond the debt, and they refer them (the settlee) to collect his share from the debtors. In this scenario there is no harm to them; because even though the amount of the debt came out from them, they nevertheless obtained the debt in return for it, so harm is eliminated except harm of postponement, because property is better than debt. And the best is that they sell something like dates or similar to the amount of the debt, then they refer them to the debtors, or they refer them initially to sell something for them to collect for him, then they take it for themselves. End as much as needed. Muhit etc.: i.e., if the deceased had a debt that encompasses the entire estate, the sulh and division are invalid, because the heirs do not own the estate in this case. If it is not encompassing, they should not divide it or make a sulh until they pay his debt. If they do so, it is permissible. And al-Karkhi mentioned regarding division: it is not permissible by istihsan, but it is permissible by qiyas. [Ramz al-Haqaiq: 2/238]
Source pages p. 88

Commentary
This passage from Kitab al-Sulh presents several rulings on compromise (sulh) in the context of estates. The text first addresses a scenario where the estate includes gold, silver, and other goods. The heirs make a sulh with one recipient by giving him either gold or silver for his share. The ruling is that this sulh is only valid if the amount given is more than his prescribed share; otherwise, it is invalid due to riba (usury) because the transaction would involve an exchange of currency without equivalence. The commentary explains that the sulh is treated as a transaction (mu'awada) rather than a discharge (ibra) because discharge applies only to debts, not physical properties. Thus, conditions of exchange must be met, including hand-to-hand exchange (taqabud) in the session for gold and silver (sarf). If the given amount is equal to or less than the share, or if the share is unknown, the sulh is corrupt. However, if the given consideration is goods (not currency), it is permissible unconditionally as riba does not apply. The second part discusses when the estate includes a debt owed by third parties. If the heirs settle by giving the debt to the settlee, making him its owner, the sulh is invalid. This is because transferring ownership of a debt to someone other than the debtor is invalid, as the debt is not a tangible object that can be possessed. A dispute is noted: according to Abu Hanifa, the entire sulh is invalid, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) hold that the sulh remains valid for the non-debt portion if the shares are specified. The analogy is drawn to selling a mixed package of a free man and a slave or a ritually slaughtered sheep and a carcass. The third part provides a valid alternative: if the heirs stipulate that the debtors be discharged from the settlee's share, the sulh is valid, as this constitutes a discharge (ibra) or assignment of the debt to the debtor. Legal stratagems (hiyal) are discussed to avoid harming other heirs, such as the heirs lending the settlee his share and then making sulh on the remaining assets, with referral to debtors. Finally, if the deceased had a debt that consumes the entire estate, the sulh and division are invalid because the heirs do not own the estate; they must pay the debt first. If the debt does not exhaust the estate, division or sulh is permissible after paying the debt, though al-Karkhi notes a difference between istihsan and qiyas regarding division.

Key Terms
صلح (sulh): A compromise or settlement in which one party relinquishes a claim in exchange for compensation.
إبراء (ibra): A unilateral discharge or release of a debt obligation.
ربا (riba): Usury or unjustified increase in financial transactions, prohibited in Sharia.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if the estate includes gold and silver, and the heirs settle with a claimant by giving him silver worth exactly his share, the sulh is:
A) Valid because the claimant's consent makes it permissible.
B) Invalid because the exchange involves riba due to lack of excess.
C) Valid if the silver is given in the same session.
D) Invalid but can be rectified by adding goods.

Key Takeaway
The condition that the given currency must exceed the settlee's share is necessary to prevent riba in sulh involving mixed assets.

Sulh Involving Debt: Invalid Transfer and Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Ruling on sulh when estate includes a debt

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why transferring a debt to the settlee in sulh is invalid according to Abu Hanifa, and contrast the view of the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
Transferring ownership of a debt to a non-debtor invalidates the sulh – Abu Hanifa holds strict, Sahibayn allow salvage.

This lesson addresses a common scenario in inheritance: the estate includes a debt owed by third parties. When the heirs try to settle by giving the debt itself to the claimant, a serious question arises. We'll dissect the Hanafi position and the internal disagreement between Abu Hanifa and his two companions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The estate includes a debt (e.g., money owed to the deceased by others). The heirs make a sulh with a claimant by transferring ownership of that debt to him.
The settlee becomes the creditor of the original debtors.
2
State Abu Hanifa's ruling
The sulh is invalid in its entirety (in both debt and non-debt assets), regardless of whether the debt's share is specified.
Abu Hanifa considers the entire contract tainted.
3
State the Sahibayn's view
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad say the sulh is valid for the non-debt portion if the debt's share is specified and separated.
They allow partial validity.
4
Analyze the basis of the dispute
Abu Hanifa analogizes to selling a debt to a third party (invalid), while Sahibayn analogize to selling a mixed package where each item's price is distinguished (valid for the permissible part).
The difference hinges on whether the contract can be split.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Under Abu Hanifa, the heirs must entirely restructure the sulh; under Sahibayn, they can salvage the non-debt assets by specifying shares.
The mufta bihi is Abu Hanifa's stricter view.

فإن كان على وجه الإخبار كقوله هو بريء من مالي قبله، فهو صحيح متناول للدين والعين، فلا تسمع الدعوى، وكذا إذا قال: لا ملك لي في هذه العين ذكره في "المبسوط" و"المحيط" ، فعلم أن قوله: لا استحق قبله حقاً مطلقاً ولا استحقاقاً، ولا دعوى يمنع الدعوى بحق من الحقوق قبل الإقرار عيناً كان أو ديناً، قال في "المبسوط": ويدخل في قوله: "لا حق لي قبل "فلان" كل عين أو دين وكل كفالة أو جناية أو إجارة أو حدّ، فإن ادعى الطالب بعد ذلك حقاً لم تقبل بينته عليه حتى يشهدوا أنه كان بعد البراءة إلخ. (فتح) وعن نقدين إلخ: أي إذا كانت التركة مشتملة على الذهب والفضة وغيرهما من العروض والعقار، فأخرجت الورثة أحدهم بأحد النقدين أي أعطوه عن نصيبه من التركة إما الذهب أو الفضة، لا يجوز هذا الصلح ما لم يكن الذي أعطوه أكثر من هذا النقد الذي دفعوه إليه؛ ليكون نصيبه بمثله، والزيادة في مقابلة حقه . التركة تحرزاً عن الربا؛ لأنه لما حمل على المعاوضة لتعذر حمله على الإبراء من الأعيان، وجب اعتبار شرط المعاوضة فيه، وذلك بما ذكرنا، وإنما تعذر الحمل على الإبراء؛ لأن الإسقاط إنما يستعمل في الديون لا في الأعيان، ولابد من التقابض في المجلس فيما يقابل من نصيبه من الذهب والفضة؛ لأنه صرف في هذا القدر، ولو كان ما أعطوه أقل أو مساوياً لنصيبه، أو لا يعلم قدر نصيبه من الدراهم، فسد الصلح.

Book of Sulh. Common debt. And regarding two currencies and other goods with one of the two currencies, it is not [valid] unless what is given is more than his share from it, and regarding one of the two currencies, i.e., the sulh is not valid in the passive form from the share of the settlee, i.e., from the kind of what is given. If it is on the basis of declaration, like his saying: he is free from any property of mine that he has, then it is valid, encompassing debt and property, and the claim is not heard. Similarly, if he says: I have no ownership in this property. It is mentioned in al-Mabsut and al-Muhit. So it is known that his saying: I have no right before him absolutely, no entitlement, and no claim, prevents the claim of any right before the acknowledgment, whether property or debt. He said in al-Mabsut: his saying 'I have no right against so-and-so' includes every property or debt, every guarantee, crime, lease, or hadd penalty. If the claimant later claims a right, his evidence is not accepted unless they testify that it was after the declaration. The estate is to avoid riba; because since it is treated as a transaction (mu'awada) due to the impossibility of treating it as a discharge (ibra') from the properties, it becomes necessary to consider the condition of transaction in it, as we mentioned. And the explanation of the corruption when they give him the amount of his right or less is that the consideration (the goods and some gold or silver) is obtained without compensation, so it becomes riba. Similarly, if his share is not known, due to the possibility of riba. Because the corruption is based on the assumption that it is equal to or less than his share, so it is more likely and more deserving of consideration. Unlike validity, which is one-sided, i.e., when what is taken is more than his share, so the consideration is for the side of corruption because it is two-sided. Commentary
This passage from Kitab al-Sulh presents several rulings on compromise (sulh) in the context of estates. The text first addresses a scenario where the estate includes gold, silver, and other goods. The heirs make a sulh with one recipient by giving him either gold or silver for his share. The ruling is that this sulh is only valid if the amount given is more than his prescribed share; otherwise, it is invalid due to riba (usury) because the transaction would involve an exchange of currency without equivalence. The commentary explains that the sulh is treated as a transaction (mu'awada) rather than a discharge (ibra) because discharge applies only to debts, not physical properties. Thus, conditions of exchange must be met, including hand-to-hand exchange (taqabud) in the session for gold and silver (sarf). If the given amount is equal to or less than the share, or if the share is unknown, the sulh is corrupt. However, if the given consideration is goods (not currency), it is permissible unconditionally as riba does not apply. The second part discusses when the estate includes a debt owed by third parties. If the heirs settle by giving the debt to the settlee, making him its owner, the sulh is invalid. This is because transferring ownership of a debt to someone other than the debtor is invalid, as the debt is not a tangible object that can be possessed. A dispute is noted: according to Abu Hanifa, the entire sulh is invalid, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) hold that the sulh remains valid for the non-debt portion if the shares are specified. The analogy is drawn to selling a mixed package of a free man and a slave or a ritually slaughtered sheep and a carcass. The third part provides a valid alternative: if the heirs stipulate that the debtors be discharged from the settlee's share, the sulh is valid, as this constitutes a discharge (ibra) or assignment of the debt to the debtor. Legal stratagems (hiyal) are discussed to avoid harming other heirs, such as the heirs lending the settlee his share and then making sulh on the remaining assets, with referral to debtors. Finally, if the deceased had a debt that consumes the entire estate, the sulh and division are invalid because the heirs do not own the estate; they must pay the debt first. If the debt does not exhaust the estate, division or sulh is permissible after paying the debt, though al-Karkhi notes a difference between istihsan and qiyas regarding division.

Key Terms
صلح (sulh): A compromise or settlement in which one party relinquishes a claim in exchange for compensation.
إبراء (ibra): A unilateral discharge or release of a debt obligation.
دين (dayn): A debt, a financial obligation that is not physically present.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi (relied-upon) position in the Hanafi school, if an estate includes a debt and the heirs transfer that debt to the settlee in a sulh, the sulh is:
A) Valid if the settlee agrees.
B) Valid for the non-debt assets if the debt's share is specified.
C) Invalid in its entirety.
D) Valid only if the debtors also consent.

Key Takeaway
Transferring a debt to the settlee in sulh invalidates the entire contract according to the Hanafi mufta bihi, due to the impossibility of owning a debt from a non-debtor.

Valid Alternatives in Sulh Involving Debt and Impact of Deceased's Debt
Valid alternatives and ruling on deceased's debt

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify valid structures for sulh when debt is present (ibra, hawala, etc.) and state the ruling when the deceased's debt engulfs the estate.

Core Idea
When debt invalidates a sulh, use ibra or hawala; if the deceased's debt covers the estate, sulh and division are invalid.

After learning that transferring a debt invalidates the sulh, you need to know what alternatives work. This lesson presents legal stratagems (hiyal) from the Hanafi school to achieve a valid settlement. It also covers the fundamental rule that if the deceased's debts exceed the estate, the heirs cannot dispose of the property at all.

Guided Path
1
Identify the problem scenario
The estate includes a debt. The heirs wish to settle with a claimant without transferring the debt. The text provides several valid structures.
The goal is to avoid the invalidity from the previous lesson.
2
First valid structure: discharge (ibra) of the debtor
If the heirs stipulate that the debtors be discharged from the settlee's share, the sulh is valid. This is because it is either ibra (discharge) or a transfer of debt to the one who owes it.
Discharge applies to debts, so it is valid.
3
Second valid structure: lending and hawala
The heirs lend the settlee his share, then make sulh on the remaining assets. They then refer the settlee to collect from the debtors (hawala). This avoids harm to other heirs.
This is a common hila recommended by the Hidaya.
4
Third valid structure: selling and hawala
The heirs sell some goods, use the proceeds to pay the settlee, and refer him to the debtors, or they refer him initially to sell something himself.
The goal is to give him a tangible asset or claim against the debtors.
5
Ruling on the deceased's debt
If the deceased had a debt that covers the entire estate, any sulh or division by the heirs is invalid. If the debt is less than the estate, the heirs should pay the debt first before dividing or settling.
The heirs do not own the estate until debts are paid.

Source Text

كتاب الصلح
الدين المشترك
وعن نقدين وغيرهما بأحد النقدين لا ما لم يكن المعطى أكثر من حظه منه، ولو في أحد النقدين أي لا يصح الصلح بصيغة المفعول من نصيب المصالح أي من جنس المعطى
بعوض
التركة دين على الناس فأخرجوه ليكون الدين لهم، بطل،
=
أي الصلح في العين والدين
فإن كان على وجه الإخبار كقوله هو بريء من مالي قبله، فهو صحيح متناول للدين والعين، فلا تسمع الدعوى، وكذا إذا قال: لا ملك لي في هذه العين ذكره في "المبسوط" و"المحيط" ، فعلم أن قوله: لا استحق قبله حقاً مطلقاً ولا استحقاقاً، ولا دعوى يمنع الدعوى بحق من الحقوق قبل الإقرار عيناً كان أو ديناً، قال في "المبسوط": ويدخل في قوله: "لا حق لي قبل "فلان" كل عين أو دين وكل كفالة أو جناية أو إجارة أو حدّ، فإن ادعى الطالب بعد ذلك حقاً لم تقبل بينته عليه حتى يشهدوا أنه كان بعد البراءة إلخ. (فتح) وعن نقدين إلخ: أي إذا كانت التركة مشتملة على الذهب والفضة وغيرهما من العروض والعقار، فأخرجت الورثة أحدهم بأحد النقدين أي أعطوه عن نصيبه من التركة إما الذهب أو الفضة، لا يجوز هذا الصلح ما لم يكن الذي أعطوه أكثر من هذا النقد الذي دفعوه إليه؛ ليكون نصيبه بمثله، والزيادة في مقابلة حقه . التركة تحرزاً عن الربا؛ لأنه لما حمل على المعاوضة لتعذر حمله على الإبراء من الأعيان، وجب اعتبار شرط المعاوضة فيه، وذلك بما ذكرنا، وإنما تعذر الحمل على الإبراء؛ لأن الإسقاط إنما يستعمل في الديون لا في الأعيان، ولابد من التقابض في المجلس فيما يقابل من نصيبه من الذهب والفضة؛ لأنه صرف في هذا القدر، ولو كان ما أعطوه أقل أو مساوياً لنصيبه، أو لا يعلم قدر نصيبه من الدراهم، فسد الصلح.

ووجه
من
حظه
من
بقية
لهم
الفساد فيما إذا أعطوه قدر حقه أو أقل كون العوض أي العروض وبعض الذهب أو الفضة حاصلاً بلا عوض، فيكون رباً، وكذا إذا لم يعلم قدر نصيبه؛ لاحتمال الربا؛ لأن الفساد على تقدير كونه مساوياً له أو أقل، فكان أرجح وأولى بالاعتبار، بخلاف الصحة؛ فإنها من جانب واحد، وهو ما إذا كان المأخوذ أكثر من نصيبه، فكانت العبرة لجانب الفساد؛ لكونه من وجهين، ولو كان ما أعطوه عرضاً جاز مطلقاً؛ لعدم الربا. (فتح عيني، ملا مسكين بتوضيح من المحشي) ولو في التركة دين إلخ: أي إن كان في التركة دين على الناس، فصالحوا على أن يخرجوا المصالح من الدين ليكون الدين لهم، بطل الصلح مطلقاً في الدين والعين، قيل: هذا قول أبي حنيفة له، وعندهما: يبقى العقد صحيحاً فيما وراء الدين وقيل: هو قول الكل. (مسكين)
بطل: أي بطل هذا الصلح؛ لأن ذلك تمليك الدين الذي هو حصة المصالح. من غيره، وتمليكه من غير من عليه الدين لا يجوز، وسواء في ذلك يبين حصة الدين أو لم يبين عند أبي حنيفة حاله، وينبغي أن يجوز عندهما في غير الدين إذا بين حصته. وأصل الخلاف فيما إذا جمع بين حر وعبد أو شاة ذكية وميتة، وباعهما في صفقة واحدة، وبين كل واحد منهما من الثمن بطل في الكل عنده وعندهما صح في العبد والذكية [رمز الحقائق: ۲۳۸/٢]

كتاب الصلح
وإن شرطوا أن
أي الورثة
۸۸
الدين المشترك
يبرء الغرماء منه صح، ولو على الميت دين محيط بطل الصلح والقسمة.
نصيب المصالح من الدين كان
بالتركة
أي قسمة الدين
وإن شرطوا إلخ الورثة في هذه المسألة أن يبرأ الغرماء منه أي من نصيب المصالح من الدين صح الصلح. (مسكين) وقال في "الفتح": لأنه إسقاط أو تمليك للدين ممن هو عليه وهذه حيلة الجواز، وأخرى أن يعجلوا قضاء نصيبه متبرعين قال في "الهداية": وفي الوجهين ضرر لبقية الورثة، والأوجه أن يقرضوا المصالح مقدار نصيبه، ويصالحوا عما وراء الدين ويحيلهم على استيفاء نصيبه من الغرماء وليس عليهم في هذه الصورة ضرر؛ لأنه وإن خرج منهم قدر الدين لكن حصل لهم الدين بمقابلته، فانتفى الضرر عنهم إلا ضرر التقديم، فإن العين خير من الدين، وأوجه أن منه من تمر أو نحوه بقدر الدين ثم يحيلهم على الغرماء، أو يحيلهم ابتداء
من
يبيعوه
كذا
غير بيع شيء ليقتضوه له ، ثم يأخذوه لأنفسهم، انتهى بقدر الضرورة. محيط إلخ أي لو كان على الميت دين مستغرق بالتركة بطل الصلح والقسمة؛ لأن الورثة لا يملكون التركة في هذه الحالة، وإن لم يكن مستغرقاً بالدين لا ينبغي لهم أن يقسموه، أو يصالحوه ما لم يقضوا دينه، وإن فعلوا ذلك جاز، وذكر الكرخي في القسمة أنها لا تجوز استحساناً وتجوز قياساً. [رمز الحقائق: ۲۳۸/٢]
Book of Sulh. Common debt. And regarding two currencies and other goods with one of the two currencies, it is not [valid] unless what is given is more than his share from it, and regarding one of the two currencies, i.e., the sulh is not valid in the passive form from the share of the settlee, i.e., from the kind of what is given. With compensation. The estate is a debt owed by the people, so they take it out to make the debt theirs; it is invalid. = i.e., the sulh regarding the property and debt. If it is on the basis of declaration, like his saying: he is free from any property of mine that he has, then it is valid, encompassing debt and property, and the claim is not heard. Similarly, if he says: I have no ownership in this property. It is mentioned in al-Mabsut and al-Muhit. So it is known that his saying: I have no right before him absolutely, no entitlement, and no claim, prevents the claim of any right before the acknowledgment, whether property or debt. He said in al-Mabsut: his saying 'I have no right against so-and-so' includes every property or debt, every guarantee, crime, lease, or hadd penalty. If the claimant later claims a right, his evidence is not accepted unless they testify that it was after the declaration. (Fath) And regarding two currencies etc.: i.e., if the estate includes gold and silver and other movable and immovable goods, and the heirs take out one of them with one of the two currencies, i.e., they give him for his share of the estate either gold or silver, this sulh is not valid unless what they give is more than the currency they paid to him; so that his share is equivalent to it, and the excess is in return for his right. The estate is to avoid riba; because since it is treated as a transaction (mu'awada) due to the impossibility of treating it as a discharge (ibra') from the properties, it becomes necessary to consider the condition of transaction in it, as we mentioned. And the impossibility of treating it as a discharge is because discharge is only used for debts, not for properties. And hand-to-hand exchange (taqabud) in the session is required for what corresponds to his share of gold and silver, because it is sarf in this amount. And if they gave him less than or equal to his share, or his share in dirhams is not known, the sulh is corrupt (fasid). And the explanation of the corruption when they give him the amount of his right or less is that the consideration (the goods and some gold or silver) is obtained without compensation, so it becomes riba. Similarly, if his share is not known, due to the possibility of riba. Because the corruption is based on the assumption that it is equal to or less than his share, so it is more likely and more deserving of consideration. Unlike validity, which is one-sided, i.e., when what is taken is more than his share, so the consideration is for the side of corruption because it is two-sided. And if what they gave is goods, it is permissible absolutely, due to the absence of riba. (Fath 'Ayni, Mulla Miskeen with clarification from the commentator) And regarding the estate is a debt etc.: i.e., if the estate includes a debt owed by the people, and they agree to take out the settlee from the debt to make the debt theirs, the sulh is invalid absolutely in the debt and property. It was said: this is the view of Abu Hanifa. And according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), the contract remains valid with respect to what is beyond the debt. And it was said: this is the view of all. (Miskeen) Batal: i.e., this sulh is invalid because it is a transfer of ownership of the debt which is the share of the settlee from someone else, and transferring ownership of it from someone other than the debtor is not permissible. And it is equal in this whether they specify the share of the debt or not, according to Abu Hanifa. And it should be permissible according to them (the two) regarding other than the debt if they specify his share. And the origin of the dispute is when one combines a free man and a slave, or a slaughtered sheep that is permissible and a dead one, and sells them in a single transaction, and distinguishes each of them from the price: according to him (Abu Hanifa) it is invalid in all, and according to them it is valid in the slave and the permissible sheep. [Ramz al-Haqaiq: 2/238] And if they stipulate that the debtors be discharged from it, it is valid. And if the deceased had a debt that engulfs the estate, the sulh and division are invalid. The share of the settlee from the debt was with the estate? i.e., division of debt. And if they stipulate etc.: the heirs in this issue that the debtors be discharged from it, i.e., from the share of the settlee from the debt, the sulh is valid. (Miskeen) And he said in al-Fath: because it is a discharge or a transfer of ownership of the debt to the one who owes it, and this is a legal stratagem (hila) for permissibility. Another stratagem is that they expedite payment of his share as a donation. He said in al-Hidaya: In both ways there is harm to the remaining heirs. The best is that they lend the settlee the amount of his share, and they make a sulh regarding what is beyond the debt, and they refer them (the settlee) to collect his share from the debtors. In this scenario there is no harm to them; because even though the amount of the debt came out from them, they nevertheless obtained the debt in return for it, so harm is eliminated except harm of postponement, because property is better than debt. And the best is that they sell something like dates or similar to the amount of the debt, then they refer them to the debtors, or they refer them initially to sell something for them to collect for him, then they take it for themselves. End as much as needed. Muhit etc.: i.e., if the deceased had a debt that encompasses the entire estate, the sulh and division are invalid, because the heirs do not own the estate in this case. If it is not encompassing, they should not divide it or make a sulh until they pay his debt. If they do so, it is permissible. And al-Karkhi mentioned regarding division: it is not permissible by istihsan, but it is permissible by qiyas. [Ramz al-Haqaiq: 2/238]
Source pages p. 88

Commentary
This passage from Kitab al-Sulh presents several rulings on compromise (sulh) in the context of estates. The text first addresses a scenario where the estate includes gold, silver, and other goods. The heirs make a sulh with one recipient by giving him either gold or silver for his share. The ruling is that this sulh is only valid if the amount given is more than his prescribed share; otherwise, it is invalid due to riba (usury) because the transaction would involve an exchange of currency without equivalence. The commentary explains that the sulh is treated as a transaction (mu'awada) rather than a discharge (ibra) because discharge applies only to debts, not physical properties. Thus, conditions of exchange must be met, including hand-to-hand exchange (taqabud) in the session for gold and silver (sarf). If the given amount is equal to or less than the share, or if the share is unknown, the sulh is corrupt. However, if the given consideration is goods (not currency), it is permissible unconditionally as riba does not apply. The second part discusses when the estate includes a debt owed by third parties. If the heirs settle by giving the debt to the settlee, making him its owner, the sulh is invalid. This is because transferring ownership of a debt to someone other than the debtor is invalid, as the debt is not a tangible object that can be possessed. A dispute is noted: according to Abu Hanifa, the entire sulh is invalid, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) hold that the sulh remains valid for the non-debt portion if the shares are specified. The analogy is drawn to selling a mixed package of a free man and a slave or a ritually slaughtered sheep and a carcass. The third part provides a valid alternative: if the heirs stipulate that the debtors be discharged from the settlee's share, the sulh is valid, as this constitutes a discharge (ibra) or assignment of the debt to the debtor. Legal stratagems (hiyal) are discussed to avoid harming other heirs, such as the heirs lending the settlee his share and then making sulh on the remaining assets, with referral to debtors. Finally, if the deceased had a debt that consumes the entire estate, the sulh and division are invalid because the heirs do not own the estate; they must pay the debt first. If the debt does not exhaust the estate, division or sulh is permissible after paying the debt, though al-Karkhi notes a difference between istihsan and qiyas regarding division.

Key Terms
صلح (sulh): A compromise or settlement in which one party relinquishes a claim in exchange for compensation.
إبراء (ibra): A unilateral discharge or release of a debt obligation.
حيلة (hila): A legal stratagem or device used to achieve a permissible outcome without violating the law.
حوالة (hawala): A transfer of a debt from one person to another, with the debtor's consent, akin to an assignment.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If the deceased's debt covers the entire value of the estate, what is the ruling on the heirs making a sulh with a creditor?
A) Valid if the creditor agrees.
B) Valid for the non-debt assets.
C) Invalid because the heirs do not own the estate.
D) Valid if they pay the debt first.

Key Takeaway
Valid sulh involving debt requires using ibra or hawala; if the deceased's debt covers the estate, the heirs cannot dispose of it at all.

Compromise of Joint Debt Among Heirs: Conditions and Ruling
Explains ruling, conditions, stratagems, and internal dispute on compromise of joint debt

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on compromise (sulh) of a joint debt among heirs and identify the condition that renders it void (batil).

Core Idea
A compromise on a deceased's debt is void if the debt engulfs the estate, because heirs do not own the property.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq explains the ruling on compromising a debt that the deceased owed, when the heirs wish to settle among themselves. It clarifies that while a compromise is generally valid, it is void when the debt encompasses the entire estate. The text also explores stratagems to avoid harming other heirs and notes an internal Hanafi dispute between istihsan and qiyas.

Guided Path
1
Identify the basic ruling
The text states that if the heirs stipulate that the creditors are discharged from the share of the compromising heir, the compromise is valid. This is the default ruling.
The stipulation effectively transfers the debt from the estate to the compromising heir.
2
Recognize the invalidating condition
If the deceased's debt encompasses (muhit) the entire estate, both compromise and division of the estate are void. The reason is that the heirs do not own the estate when all its value is consumed by debt.
Encompassing means the debt equals or exceeds the total value of the estate.
3
Understand permissible stratagems
To avoid harm to other heirs, various stratagems (hiyal) are discussed: voluntary payment, lending, or selling goods to the compromising heir. The preferred method minimizes harm while allowing compromise.
The text cautions that any stratagem may still cause harm (e.g., having a debt instead of cash).
4
Analyze the internal ikhtilaf
Al-Karkhi reports that division of the estate before debt payment is not valid by istihsan (juristic preference) but is valid by qiyas (analogy). The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is istihsan, to prevent harm to creditors.
This dispute is within the Hanafi school; the principle of istihsan overrides strict analogy when hardship arises.

Source Text

أي قسمة الدين
وإن شرطوا إلخ الورثة في هذه المسألة أن يبرأ الغرماء منه أي من نصيب المصالح من الدين صح الصلح. (مسكين) وقال في "الفتح": لأنه إسقاط أو تمليك للدين ممن هو عليه وهذه حيلة الجواز، وأخرى أن يعجلوا قضاء نصيبه متبرعين قال في "الهداية": وفي الوجهين ضرر لبقية الورثة، والأوجه أن يقرضوا المصالح مقدار نصيبه، ويصالحوا عما وراء الدين ويحيلهم على استيفاء نصيبه من الغرماء وليس عليهم في هذه الصورة ضرر؛ لأنه وإن خرج منهم قدر الدين لكن حصل لهم الدين بمقابلته، فانتفى الضرر عنهم إلا ضرر التقديم، فإن العين خير من الدين، وأوجه أن منه من تمر أو نحوه بقدر الدين ثم يحيلهم على الغرماء، أو يحيلهم ابتداء

يبيعوه
كذا
غير بيع شيء ليقتضوه له ، ثم يأخذوه لأنفسهم، انتهى بقدر الضرورة. محيط إلخ أي لو كان على الميت دين مستغرق بالتركة بطل الصلح والقسمة؛ لأن الورثة لا يملكون التركة في هذه الحالة، وإن لم يكن مستغرقاً بالدين لا ينبغي لهم أن يقسموه، أو يصالحوه ما لم يقضوا دينه، وإن فعلوا ذلك جاز، وذكر الكرخي في القسمة أنها لا تجوز استحساناً وتجوز قياساً. [رمز الحقائق: ۲۳۸/۲]
The Book of Compromise. And if they stipulate that the creditors are discharged from it, it is valid. And if the deceased has a debt encompassing the estate, the compromise and division are void. (Explanation): The share of the one making the compromise from the debt from the estate—i.e., the division of the debt. And if they stipulate... etc. The heirs in this issue that the creditors are discharged from it, i.e., from the share of the one making the compromise from the debt, the compromise is valid. (Miskin) And it is said in al-Fath: Because it is a relinquishment or transfer of the debt to the one who owes it, and this is a permissible stratagem. Another (stratagem) is that they hasten to pay his share voluntarily. It is said in al-Hidayah: In both methods there is harm to the remaining heirs. The most appropriate is that they lend to the one making the compromise the amount of his share, and they compromise regarding what is beyond the debt, and they transfer (the claim) to him for collecting his share from the creditors. In this form there is no harm to them; because although the amount of the debt leaves them, they acquire the debt in return, so harm is removed from them except the harm of priority, for cash is better than a debt. And the most appropriate is that he sells them dates or the like to the amount of the debt, then transfers them to the creditors, or transfers them initially to someone else to sell it... etc. So that they may collect it for him, then take it for themselves. End. (Muhit etc.) That is, if the deceased has a debt engulfing the estate, the compromise and division are void, because the heirs do not own the estate in this case. And if it is not engulfing by the debt, they should not divide it or compromise until they pay his debt. If they do so, it is permissible. Al-Karkhi mentioned regarding division that it is not permissible by istihsan but permissible by qiyas.
Source pages p. 89

Commentary
This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq's commentary addresses the ruling on compromise (sulh) of a joint debt among heirs. The author begins by stating the basic ruling: if the heirs stipulate that the creditors are discharged from the share of the one making the compromise, it is valid. However, if the deceased's debt encompasses the entire estate, both the compromise and the division of the estate are void because the heirs do not actually own the estate. The commentary then explores stratagems to avoid harming the other heirs, as discussed in al-Fath and al-Hidayah. Three methods are mentioned: (1) the other heirs voluntarily pay the compromising heir's share, (2) they lend him his share, and (3) they sell him goods on credit equal to his share and then transfer the claim to the creditors. The preferred method is the one that minimizes harm, though there is always the disadvantage of having a debt rather than cash. Finally, Al-Karkhi's view is noted: by istihsan (juristic preference) division is not valid, but by qiyas (analogy) it is valid. The relied-upon position in the Hanafi school is that such division is invalid when the debt is engulfing.

Key Terms
الصحلح (al-sulh): A contract of compromise settling a dispute or claim by mutual agreement, often involving a transfer or relinquishment of rights.
الدين المشترك (al-dayn al-mushtarak): A debt owed jointly to multiple creditors or by multiple debtors; here specifically a debt on the deceased that is shared among the heirs.
محيط (muhit): A debt that encompasses the entire estate, meaning the total debt equals or exceeds the total value of the estate.
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference based on equity, overriding strict analogy (qiyas) to avoid hardship.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When does a compromise (sulh) regarding a debt of the deceased become void?
A) When the heirs disagree among themselves.
B) When the debt encompasses the entire estate.
C) When the debt is less than the estate.
D) When the compromise involves a transfer of debt.

Key Takeaway
The validity of compromise among heirs hinges on whether the debt encompasses the estate; if it does, the compromise is void regardless of agreement.

Mudarib's Includable Expenses in Murabahah Sale
Ruling on mudarib's cost basis in Murabahah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle to identify which expenses a mudarib may include in the cost price when selling on Murabahah.

Core Idea
Only expenses that increase the goods' value are included; personal expenses are not.

When a mudarib sells merchandise on a cost-plus basis (Murabahah), the buyer is entitled to know the true cost. This lesson clarifies the Hanafi rule that only expenditures that enhance the value of the goods—whether directly (e.g., dyeing) or indirectly (e.g., transport)—are added to the cost. Expenses incurred for the mudarib's own benefit are excluded.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Sale Type
Recognize that the mudarib is selling a commodity via Murabahah, where the cost price must be disclosed to the buyer.
2
Classify Expenses
Separate expenses into two categories: those spent on the goods (e.g., tailoring, dyeing, carriage) and those spent on the mudarib himself (e.g., food, lodging).
This is the core distinction drawn in the text.
3
Apply the Value-Increase Principle
Determine which expenses cause an increase in the market value of the goods – either in reality (physical improvement) or in effect (necessary for sale, like broker fees). Include those.
Customary trade expenses are considered value-increasing by analogy.
4
Handle Travel Context
Observe that expenses incurred during travel for the mudaraba are treated differently depending on location: if the mudarib is in his home town, he cannot spend from capital; while traveling, he can, but these are personal and not added to cost.
The passage uses Basra and Kufa as examples of homeland vs. travel destination.
5
Note the Ikhtilaf
Be aware that there is a minor intra-Hanafi dispute regarding medical and oil expenses (covered in a separate lesson).

Source Text

فإن باع المتاع مرابحة، حسب ما أنفق على المتاع لا على نفسه، ولو قصره، أو حمله بماله، ما أنفق المضارب الثوب المتاع الذي اشتراه حتى يأتي البصرة؛ لأن خروجه لأجل المال، ولا ينفق من المال ما دام بالبصرة؛ لأن البصرة وطن أصلي له، فكان إقامته فيه لأجل الوطن لا لأجل المال، فإذا خرج من البصرة له أن ينفق من المال إلى أن يأتي الكوفة؛ لأن خروجه من البصرة لأجل المال وله أن ينفق أيضاً ما أقام بالكوفة حتى يعود إلى البصرة؛ لأن وطنه بالكوفة كان وطن إقامة وإنه يبطله بالسفر. (فتح) كالدواء إلخ : أي نفقة المضارب إذا عمل في المصر أو في قرية في مال نفسه كالدواء؛ فإنه في ماله مطلقا، وعن أبي حنيفة محله : أن الدواء في مال المضاربة؛ لأنه لإصلاح بدنه، وكذلك النورة والدهن في قولهما، خلافا لمحمد في الدهن ووجه ظاهر الرواية كما ذكره الزيلعي : أن النفقة معلوم وقوعها، والحاجة إلى الدواء من العوارض، فكان موهوماً، فلا يجب كما في حق المرأة. (فتح) من مال فإن ربح إلخ [سواء كان في السفر أو الحضر أي فإن ربح المضارب بعد ما أنفق من رأس المال على نفسه أخذ المالك قدر ما أنفق المضارب من رأس المال حتى يتم به رأس المال، فإذا استوفى رأس المال، وفضل شيء، يكون بينهما على ما شرطا فتكون النفقة مصروفة إلى الربح؛ لأن ما أنفقه يجعل كالهالك، والهالك يصرف إلى الربح، ولا تكون مصروفة إلى رأس المال؛ لأن رأس المال أصل والربح تبع، فلا يسلم لهما التبع حتى يسلم لرب المال الأصل، وفي قوله: "فإن ربح" إشارة إلى أن للمضارب أن ينفق على نفسه المضاربة في السفر قبل الربح، وإلى أنه لو لم يظهر ربح لا شيء على المضارب. (ملتقط من الشروح) ما أنفق إلخ : قيد بالنفقة؛ لأنه لو كان في المال دين غيرها، قدم إيفاؤه على رأس المال، كما إذا استدان المضارب بإذن صريح من رب المال، أو اشترى شيئاً بأكثر من رأس المال. (فتح) فإن باع المتاع إلخ: المراد من إنفاق المضارب مثل الحملان وأجرة السمسار والقصار والصباغ ونحوه، ويقول: قام علي بكذا، والأصل: أن ما يوجب زيادة في رأس المال حقيقة أو حكما يضمه إلى رأس المال، وكذا ما اعتاده التجار كأجرة السمسار، كذا في "النهاية". [البحر الرائق: ۳۸۹/۷] أنفق من أجرة الحمل والطراز وأجرة السمسار والصباغ والقصار ونحو ذلك مما مر ذكره في باب المرابحة. (عيني) لا على نفسه أي لا يحسب نفقة نفسه إذا باع مرابحة والفرق أن الأول يوجب زيادة في المالية بزيادة القيمة، والثاني لا يوجبها [البحر الرائق: ۳۸۹/۷]
If he sells the goods on a cost-plus basis, he calculates what he spent on the goods, not on himself. Even if he cuts it or carries it with his own wealth, the mudarib (spends on) the garment he bought until he comes to Basra because his travel is for the capital. He does not spend from the capital as long as he is in Basra because Basra is his original homeland... (Fath) 'what he spent etc.': restricted to expense because if there is a debt other than it, its repayment is given precedence over capital, as when the mudarib borrows with explicit permission from the owner, or buys something for more than the capital. (Fath) 'If he sells the goods etc.': what is meant by the mudarib's expenditure such as loading, broker's fee, tailoring, dyeing, and the like, and he says: 'it cost me such-and-such.' The principle is that whatever causes an increase in the capital, in reality or in effect, is added to the capital, and likewise what merchants customarily do, like broker's fee, as in al-Nihayah. [al-Bahr al-Ra'iq: 7/389] He spent from loading, embroidery, broker's fee, dyeing, tailoring, and the like mentioned in the chapter of Murabahah. (Ayni) 'not on himself' i.e., he does not count his own expense when selling on Murabahah. The difference is that the first causes an increase in value by increasing the price, while the second does not cause it. [al-Bahr al-Ra'iq: 7/389]
Source pages p. 106

Commentary
This passage provides the ruling on what the mudarib can include as cost when selling goods on a Murabahah (cost-plus) basis. The principle is that only expenses that increase the value of the goods—either in reality (e.g., dyeing, tailoring) or in effect (e.g., carriage, broker's fee)—are added to the cost price. Personal expenses of the mudarib, such as his own travel costs or meals, are not included because they do not enhance the value of the merchandise. The commentary from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq and al-Ayni confirms that customary trade expenses like loading charges and broker fees are included. This distinction ensures that the profit calculation is fair: the buyer pays only for the actual added value, not for the mudarib's personal upkeep.

Key Terms
مرابحة (murabahah): A sale where the seller discloses the cost price and adds a stated profit margin.
حملان (himlān): Carriage/transport charges for goods.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following expenses can a mudarib include in the cost price when selling goods on Murabahah?
A) His own food expenses during the business trip.
B) Broker's fee for finding the buyer.
C) Rent for his personal accommodation.
D) All of the above.

Key Takeaway
The mudarib must only disclose expenses that enhance the goods' value; personal costs are never part of the Murabahah cost.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
8 min
Possession in the Gift Gathering: Hanafi vs Shafi'i
Ruling on possession in hiba with and without permission

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school validates possession in the gift-giving gathering without explicit permission and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument using qiyas and istihsan.

Core Idea
Possession in the gathering substitutes for acceptance; the offer itself implies permission.

When someone receives a gift during a gathering and takes it without the donor's explicit permission, is the gift valid? The Hanafis say yes, based on juristic preference (istihsan), while the Shafi'is say no, following strict analogy (qiyas). This lesson unpacks the reasoning behind each position and the practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify that the Hanafi school holds the gift valid when the donee takes possession in the gathering (majlis) without the donor's explicit permission.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Note that Imam al-Shafi'i argues that possession without permission is invalid because it is a disposal in another's property.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Understand the Shafi'i qiyas: the asl is the general rule that disposing of another's property requires permission; the far' is possession of a gift; the illa is the act of disposal.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
See how the Hanafis use istihsan: possession in the gathering is like acceptance; the offer itself grants authority to take possession.
The offer is an implied permission within the gathering.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: in the Hanafi school, the donee owns the gift immediately upon possession; in the Shafi'i school, ownership is not transferred until the donor explicitly allows it.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقبض في المجلس بلا إذنه وبعده به في محوز مقسوم ومشاع لا يقسم لا فيما قسم أي الواهب أي بعد المجلس = من كالدار مثلا " وكان من قوله: لو قال: قد وهبت جاريتي هذه لأحدكم فليأخذها . شاء، فأخذها رجل منهم . تكون له"، أخذه قبولاً، وما في "المحيط" من أنها تدل على أنه لا يشترط في الهبة القبول مشكل [البحر الرائق: ٤١٤/٧] وقبض إلخ : أي لابد من القبض فيها؛ لثبوت الملك لا للصحة والتمكن من القبض كالقبض، فلو وهب لرجل ثيابا في صندوق مقفل، ودفع إليه الصندوق لم يكن قبضاً، وإن كان مفتوحاً كان قبضاً لتمكنه منه. البحر الرائق: ٤١٤/٧] ولو نهاه عن القبض لم يصح قبضه مطلقاً ولو في المجلس؛ لأن الصريح أقوى من الدلالة تنوير وشرحه) واعلم أن اشتراط الإذن للقبض في غير المجلس مخالف لظاهر ما في التتارخانية، ونصه قال أبو بكر : إذا قال الرجل لغيره: وهبت عبدي منك، والعبد غائب، فذهب وقبضه، ولم يقل: قبلت، جازت الهبة، قال أبو الليث وبقول أبي بكر نأخذ. (فتح) بلا إذنه: أي تصح الهبة إن قبض بلا إذنه إذا كان في المجلس، والقياس أن لا يجوز بلا إذنه؛ لأنه تصرف في ملك الغير، فلا يجوز إلا بإذنه وبه قال الشافعي وجه الاستحسان أن القبض كالقبول في الهبة من حيث إنه يتوقف عليه ثبوت حكمه، وهو الملك، فيكون الإيجاب منه تسليطاً على القبض، فكما لا يشترط للقبول إذنه بعد الإيجاب، فكذا القبض في المجلس. رمز الحقائق: ٢٦٠/٢] (فتح) وبعده به: أي يصح بعد المجلس، أراد بعد الافتراق "به" أي بالإذن فلا تصح بعد الافتراق بلا إذن؛ لأنا أثبتنا التسليط فيه إلحاقاً له بالقبول، وهو يتقيد بالمجلس؛ لأن الدلالة لا تعمل في مقابلة الصريح.
And possession [qabd] in the gathering without his permission, and after it with it, in what is enclosed and divided, and undivided [musha'] that cannot be divided, not in what is divided — i.e., the donor after the gathering. ... For example, from his statement: 'If he said: I have given this slave-girl of mine to one of you, so let him take her,' etc. ... The gist: possession is necessary in it [hiba] for the establishment of ownership, not for validity. And the ability to take possession is like possession itself. If he gives a garment in a locked chest and hands over the chest, it is not possession; if it is open, it is possession due to being able to take it. And if he forbids him from possession, his possession is absolutely invalid even in the gathering, because the explicit is stronger than implication. ... Know that stipulating permission for possession outside the gathering contradicts what appears in al-Tatarkhaniyyah, where Abu Bakr said: 'If a person says to another: I have gifted my slave to you, and the slave is absent, and he goes and seizes him without saying I accept, the gift is valid.' Abu al-Layth said: 'We take by the statement of Abu Bakr.' (Fath) Without his permission: i.e., the gift is valid if he takes possession without his permission when in the gathering. Analogy dictates it is not permissible without permission, because it is a disposal in another's property, so it is not permissible except with his permission — and al-Shafi'i said this. The basis of istihsan is that possession in hiba is like acceptance in that the ruling (ownership) depends on it, so the offer from him is a grant of authority over possession; just as permission is not required for acceptance after the offer, so too possession in the gathering. (Ramz al-Haqaiq) And after it with it: i.e., it is valid after the gathering — he meant after separation "with it" i.e., with permission. So it is not valid after separation without permission, because we established the authority therein by analogy to acceptance, and it is confined to the gathering because implication does not operate against the explicit.
Source pages p. 130

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafis and al-Shafi'i regarding possession (qabd) in gift (hiba). The Hanafi position, based on istihsan, holds that possession in the gathering (majlis) does not require the donor's explicit permission because the offer itself implies permission, just as acceptance does not require separate permission. Al-Shafi'i argues by strict analogy (qiyas) that possession without permission is invalid, as it is a disposal in another's property. The Hanafis respond that the offer grants authority, and since possession is like acceptance in effect, it is permissible in the gathering. After separation, however, permission is required because the implication (dalalah) of the offer does not extend beyond the gathering. The text also clarifies that possession of an item in a locked chest is not valid possession until the chest is opened, as the ability to take actual control is necessary. Internal Hanafi differences: Abu Bakr al-Razi and Abu al-Layth al-Samarqandi hold that possession without utterance of acceptance is sufficient even when the slave is absent, while al-Tatarkhaniyyah indicates the contrary. The relied-upon position is that possession in the gathering substitutes for acceptance.

Key Terms
قبض (qabd): Taking physical possession or control of the gifted item, which is a condition for ownership in hiba according to Hanafis.
استحسان (istihsan): A juristic preference that overrides qiyas jali (obvious analogy) based on a stronger or more appropriate inference.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on taking possession of a gift in the gathering (majlis) without the donor's explicit permission?
A) The gift is invalid because permission is required.
B) The gift is valid because the offer implies permission, similar to acceptance.
C) The gift is valid only if the donor is present.
D) The gift is valid only if the item is divisible.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school validates possession in the gift-gathering without explicit permission because the offer implies permission, but after separation explicit permission is required.
